Pledge by Special Parties: Authority Determines Validity
Rulings on pledge by parties with limited agency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings for pledge (rahn) by a mukatib, ma'dhun, mudarib, and partners, and identify the conditions of authority that affect validity.

Core Idea
The validity of a pledge by a special party hinges on the authority granted.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on rulings not explicitly covered in the matn (Kanz al-Daqa'iq). It draws from al-Mabsut to address pledges by parties with limited agency: a mukatib (slave under manumission contract), a ma'dhun (trading slave), a mudarib (qirad agent), and partners in mufawada and 'inan partnerships. The rulings vary based on the degree of authority each party possesses over the property being pledged.

Guided Path
1
Identify each party and their legal capacity
List the four types: mukatib (free-like for property), ma'dhun (trading slave), mudarib (agent with limited authority), and partners (mufawada vs 'inan). Note the legal status of each.
Mukatib and ma'dhun have full capacity over their property; mudarib's authority depends on the owner's instructions.
2
Determine the ruling for the mukatib and ma'dhun
Both are treated like free persons in pledging and taking pledges – their pledge is valid (sahih) without restriction.
No external authorization is required beyond their general capacity.
3
Analyze the mudarib's pledge
Distinguish three scenarios based on the owner's orders: (a) order to borrow and pledge, (b) order to borrow only, (c) order to pledge only, (d) no order. State the ruling for each.
If only borrowing is ordered, the pledge is invalid (fāsid) in the mudaraba share and thus wholly invalid.
4
Analyze the partner's pledge
For mufawada partners, a pledge for a crime debt is valid and the pledgor is personally liable. For 'inan partners, the ruling depends on authorization: if each works independently, one partner's pledge binds the other; if they work jointly, only the partner who conducted the lending can validly pledge.
'Inan partners need explicit mutual authority for pledging partnership property.
5
Identify the legal effects of an invalid pledge (fāsid)
Although the pledge is invalid, it can still produce some legal effects – the pledgee may be treated as a constructive collector of the debt, and the pledgor may become liable for the partner's share if the property perishes.
The passage ends with 'Isa ibn Aban's objection and a rebuttal, illustrating the nuanced Hanafi reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يتعرض المؤلف رحمه الله تعالى لرهن المكاتب والمأذون والمضارب وأحد الشريكين ففي المبسوط : المكاتب كالحر في الرهن والارتهان ورهن العبد التاجر وارتهانه جائز ورهن المضارب على أقسام إما أن يكون رب المال أمره بالاستدانة ولم يأمره بالرهن أو بالعكس أو أمره بهما، فإن أمره بالاستدانة فالرهن جائز . وتفسير الاستدانة أن يشتري بالنسيئة على المضاربة ولم يبق من رأس المال شيء، فإن صار مال المضاربة كله عروضاً، فإذا بقي شيء من رأس المال لا يكون مستديناً على المضاربة ويجوز على وجه الشركة لا على وجه المضاربة ولا يستدين من قبل أن يقبض رأس المال، وإذا رهن به شيئاً من مال المضاربة بأمر رب المال جاز، وإن لم يأمره رب المال بالاستدانة لا يجوز، وإن أمره بالاستدانة ولم يأمره بالرهن فالاستدانة جائزة والرهن فاسدة في نصيب المضاربة لأنه رهن مال المضاربة عن مال نفسه، وإذا فسد في نصيبه فسد في الكل، وإن أمره بالرهن ولم يأمره بالاستدانة فالاستدانة تلزم المضارب خاصة والرهن يكون جائزاً ورهن أحد شريكي المفاوضة بدين جناية جائز وهو ضامن وليس لشريكه أن ينقض وأحد شريكي العنان إذا متاعاً من الشركة فهو على قسمين: إما إن رهن أو ارتهن، وكل قسم لا يخلو من أوجه : إما إن رهن بدين عليها فإن اشتركا على أن يعمل كل واحد منهما برأي نفسه فرهن أحدهما وارتهانه جائز على صاحبه في الأمول كلها وإن اشتركا على أن يعملا معاً وأن يبيعا معاً أو متفرقاً إن ولى الإدانة بنفسه يجوز رهنه على صاحبه لأن له أن يقضي هذا الدين من مال الشركة لأنه هو المطالب بهذا الدين، وإذا أدان صاحبه أو أدائهما جميعاً في نصيب صاحبه لأنه رهن نصيب صاحبه بدين صاحبه بغير إذنه، وإذا لم يجز في نصيب صاحبه لا يجوز في نصيبه لأن نصيبه مشاع ويضمن نصيب صاحبه إن هلك. وهذا كله إذا كان الشريك راهناً، أحدهما بدين لهما ولم يشتركا في الشركة أن يعمل كل واحد منهما برأيه إن ولي هو الاستدانة بنفسه يجوز ارتهانه لأنه ملك استيفاء هذا الدين لأنه وجب بعقده فيملك الارتهان به لأنه استيفاء حكماً، وإن ولي الإدانة صاحبه أو ولياً الإدانة بأنفسهما لا يجوز في نصيب صاحبه لأنه لا يملك استيفاء نصيب صاحبه فلا يملك الارتهان لنفسه، وإن لم يجز في نصيب صاحبه لا يجوز في نصيبه أيضاً لأنه مشاع وإن هلك المرتهن ذهب حصته من الدين ويرجع شريكه بحصته على المطلوب، وإن شاء رجع بها على صاحبه لأن الرهن الفاسد في حق إفادة الأحكام ملحق بالصحيح فصار المرتهن مستوفياً الدين فصار مستوفياً نصيب صاحبه بغير إذنه بالهلاك فصار كما لو استوفي حقه والدين واجب بإدانة صاحبه فلصاحبه أخذ نصف الدين منه، وإن شاء أخذ من المطلوب فكذا هذا، فإذا أخذ من المطلوب يرجع المطلوب على المرتهن بنصف قيمة الرهن طعن عيسى وقال : وجب أن لا يرجع لأن المرتهن أجنبي في نصيب صاحبه ولهذا لا يبرأ المطلوب من حصة صاحبه فصار كما لو دفع الغريم رهناً إلى الأجنبي آخر ليجيز صاحب الدين ولم يجز وقد هلك في يده لم يضمن فكذا هذا. والجواب عنه أن المرتهن صار مستوفياً نصيب نفسه وصح استيفاؤه واستوفى نصيب صاحبه بغير إذنه فصار مضموناً عليه لأنا لو جعلناه أمانة في يده كان لصاحبه أن يشاركه فيما استوفاه لنفسه، وإذا شاركه فيه وأخذ منه كان للقابض أن يرجع فيما كان أمانة في يده ابتداء، فإذا أخذ ذلك كان لشريكه أن يأخذ منه نصف ذلك بنصف ما بقي ثم وثم إلى أن لا
And the author, may Allah have mercy on him, did not address the pledge of the mukatib, the ma'dhun, the mudarib, and one of the two partners. In al-Mabsut: The mukatib is like a free person in pledging and taking a pledge, and the pledge of the trading slave and his taking a pledge is permissible. The pledge of the mudarib is of types: either the owner of the capital ordered him to borrow and did not order him to pledge, or the opposite, or ordered him to both. If he ordered him to borrow, the pledge is permissible. The interpretation of borrowing is that he buys on credit for the mudaraba and nothing remains of the capital. If the mudaraba property becomes all goods, and if something remains of the capital, he is not considered a borrower for the mudaraba. It is permissible on the basis of partnership, not on the basis of mudaraba. He does not borrow before receiving the capital. If he pledges something from the mudaraba property by order of the owner of the capital, it is permissible. If the owner did not order him to borrow, it is not permissible. If he ordered him to borrow but did not order him to pledge, the borrowing is permissible and the pledge is invalid in the mudaraba share because he pledges mudaraba property for his own debt. If it is invalid in his share, it is invalid in the whole. If he ordered him to pledge but did not order him to borrow, the borrowing is binding on the mudarib specifically and the pledge is permissible. The pledge of one of the partners in a mufawada partnership for a crime debt is permissible, and he is a guarantor, and his partner cannot annul it. One of the partners in an inan partnership, if [they] refuse from the partnership, it is of two types: either he pledges or takes a pledge. Each type is not free from aspects: If he pledges for a debt upon it, if they partnered on the condition that each works with his own opinion, then if one of them pledges and takes a pledge, it is permissible on his partner in all properties. If they partnered on the condition that they work together and sell together or separately, if he undertakes the lending himself, his pledge is permissible on his partner because he can pay this debt from partnership property because he is the one demanded for this debt. If his partner lends or both lend, it is not permissible in his partner's share because he pledges his partner's share for his partner's debt without permission. If it is not permissible in his partner's share, it is not permissible in his own share because his share is common, and he guarantees his partner's share if it perishes. All this is if the partner is the pledgor. [If] one of them [pledges] for a debt owed to both, and they did not partner in the partnership that each works with his own opinion, if he himself undertakes the lending, his taking a pledge is permissible because he owns the collection of this debt since it is owed by his contract, so he owns taking a pledge for it because it is constructive collection. If his partner undertakes the lending or both undertake the lending, it is not permissible in his partner's share because he does not own collection of his partner's share, so he does not own taking a pledge for himself. If it is not permissible in his partner's share, it is also not permissible in his own share because it is common. If the pledgee [the partner] perishes, his portion of the debt is lost, and his partner sues for his portion against the debtor. If he wishes, he sues for it against his partner, because the invalid pledge in terms of effecting rulings is treated as valid, so the pledgee becomes a collector of the debt, so he becomes a collector of his partner's share without permission by the destruction, so it is as if he collected his right, and the debt is obligatory by his partner's lending, so his partner may take half of the debt from him. If he wishes, he takes from the debtor, so likewise here. When he takes from the debtor, the debtor sues the pledgee for half the value of the pledge. Eisa objected and said: It follows that he should not sue because the pledgee is a stranger regarding his partner's share, and therefore the debtor is not freed from his partner's portion, so it is as if the debtor gave a pledge to a third party for the creditor to approve, and he did not approve, and it perished in his hand – he is not liable. So likewise here. The answer to it is that the pledgee became a collector of his own portion and his collection is valid, and he collected his partner's portion without permission, so it becomes guaranteed upon him, because if we made it a trust in his hand, his partner could share with him in what he collected for himself. And if he shares with him in it and takes from him, the recipient can sue for what was a trust in his hand initially. When he takes that, his partner can take half of that, then half of what remains, then so on until there is nothing left.
Source pages p. 477

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq covers rulings on pledge by parties not explicitly discussed in the original matn (Kanz al-Daqa'iq). The author draws from al-Mabsut. First, a mukatib (slave with a contract of manumission) is like a free person in pledging and taking pledges – he has legal capacity regarding his property. A trading slave (ma'dhun) also has valid pledge transactions. For the mudarib (agent in a qirad partnership), the validity of his pledge depends on the owner's instructions. If the owner ordered borrowing (istidana) without specifying a pledge, the mudarib can pledge mudaraba property for the debt, but only if no capital remains. If the owner did not order borrowing, pledging is invalid. If the owner ordered both, it is valid. If he ordered borrowing but not pledging, the pledge is invalid in the mudaraba share and thus wholly invalid. If he ordered pledging but not borrowing, the borrowing burdens the mudarib alone, but the pledge is valid. For partners: in a mufawada (unlimited partnership), a partner's pledge for a crime debt is valid and he is personally liable; the partner cannot annul it. In an inan (limited partnership), if each works independently, a partner's pledge and taking a pledge for a debt on the partnership is valid against the partner. If they work jointly, and one partner undertakes lending, his pledge is valid; if the other partner lends, the pledge is invalid in the other's share. When a partner takes a pledge without permission, if the pledged property perishes, the pledgee becomes a constructive collector of the full debt, so his partner can recover his share from the pledgee or from the debtor. The passage ends with an objection by 'Isa ibn Aban and a rebuttal, showing the rigorous Hanafi legal reasoning.

Key Terms
المكاتب (al-mukatib): A slave who has entered into a contract of manumission (kitaba) and thus has legal capacity over his property within limits.
المضارب (al-mudarib): The agent in a qirad (mudaraba) partnership, entrusted with capital to trade.
شركة المفاوضة (sharikat al-mufawada): An unlimited partnership where partners are equal in capital, profit, and liability, and can act independently.
شركة العنان (sharikat al-'inan): A limited partnership where partners contribute capital but may have unequal shares and limited agency.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a mudarib pledges mudaraba property for a debt without the owner's order to borrow, what is the ruling?
A) The pledge is valid if the mudarib uses his own property
B) The pledge is invalid entirely
C) The pledge is valid only in the mudaraba share
D) The pledge is valid with the owner's ratification

Key Takeaway
The validity of a pledge by a mudarib or partner depends on prior authorization; without it, the pledge is invalid but may still create liability.

Liability When Pawn is Claimed After Destruction
Ruling and ta'lil for pawn death with claim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability when a pawn dies and is claimed, and explain the distinction based on which party pays the claimant.

Core Idea
If claimant sues mortgagee, mortgagee recovers value and debt; if he sues pawner, debt is satisfied.

This lesson examines a scenario where a pawned item perishes in the mortgagee's custody, and a third party subsequently claims ownership. The Hanafi school presents a nuanced ruling that depends on which party compensates the claimant. We will unpack the reasoning involving ownership transfer, deception (ghurur), and the analogy to an agent's purchase.

Guided Path
1
State the two scenarios
Note the two possibilities: claimant sues pawner, or claimant sues mortgagee. Each triggers a different liability outcome.
Keep track of who ultimately bears the loss.
2
Trace ownership sequence
When pawner pays, ownership traces back to before the pawn, so pawner is deemed owner at time of death. When mortgagee pays, ownership first passes to mortgagee, then to pawner.
This sequence is crucial for the ruling.
3
Identify the deception (ghurur) element
Mortgagee pays the claimant due to deception by pawner in delivering the item as pawn. This justifies mortgagee's recourse against pawner.
Ghurur is the basis for mortgagee's recovery of the value.
4
Contrast with Abu Hazim's objection
Abu Hazim argued that since ultimate liability is on pawner, ownership should revert to pawner directly, discharging the debt. The Hanafi response uses the agent analogy to show ownership passes through mortgagee first.
Understand why the objection is rejected.
5
Apply the analogy of the purchasing agent
Like an agent who buys from a usurper and transfers to principal, the mortgagee acquires first and then transfers to pawner. Thus pawner's ownership is later than the pawn contract.
This qiyas solidifies the Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن مات الرهن عند المرتهن فاستحق وضمن الراهن قيمته مات بالدين وإن ضمن المرتهن رجع على الراهن بالقيمة وبدينه . والأصل فيه أن العبد المرهون إذا هلك في يد المرتهن ثم استحقه رجل كان المستحق بالخيار إن شاء ضمن الراهن وإن شاء ضمن المرتهن لأن كل واحد منهما متعد في حقه الراهن بالأخذ والتسليم والمرتهن بالقبض والتسليم فإن ضمن الراهن صار المرتهن مستوفياً لدينه بهلاك الرهن لأن الراهن ملكه بأداء الضمان مسنداً إلى ما قبل التسليم فتبين أنه ملك نفسه ثم صار المرتهن مستوفياً بهلاكه، وإن ضمن المرتهن يرجع بما ضمن من القيمة وبدينه على الراهن ؛ أما بالقيمة فلأنه مغرور من جهة الراهن، وأما بالدين فلأنه انتقض قضاؤه فيعود حقه كما كان. فإن قيل : لما كان قرار الضمان على الراهن برجوع المرتهن عليه الملك في المضمون ثبت لمن عليه قرار الضمان فتبين أنه رهن ملك نفسه فصار كما إذا ضمن المستحق ابتداء قلنا : هذا طعن أبي حازم القاضي. والجواب عنه أن المرتهن يرجع على الراهن بسبب الغرور والغرور بالتسليم للمرتهن ويملك الراهن العين من ذلك الوقت وعقد الرهن كان سابقاً عليه فلم يبين أنه رهن ملك نفسه بل رهن ملكاً لغيره فلا يكون المرتهن مستوفياً بملك العين، ولأن الراهن يملك العين بالتلقي من المرتهن لأن المرتهن يملك أولاً بأداء الضمان ثم ينتقل إلى الراهن كما في الوكيل بالشراء كأن المشتري اشتراه من المستحق. وإنما كان كذلك لأن المرتهن غاصب في حق المستحق، فإذا ضمن يملك المضمون ضرورة لكيلا يجتمع البدلان في ملك واحد ثم الراهن يتلقاه فيكون ملكه بعده وعقد الرهن سابق عليه فتبين أنه رهن ملك غيره فلا يكون المرتهن مستوفياً بالهلاك بخلاف المسألة الأولى وهو ما إذا ضمن المستحق الراهن ابتداء لأنه يضمنه منه باعتبار القبض السابق على الرهن فيستند الملك إليه فتبين أنه رهن ملك نفسه فيكون المرتهن مستوفياً والله أعلم.
And if the pawn dies in the possession of the mortgagee, and then it is claimed (by a third party) and the pawner pays its value, it dies against the debt; and if the mortgagee pays, he recovers from the pawner the value and his debt. The basis of this is that if the mortgaged slave dies in the possession of the mortgagee, and then a person claims it, the claimant has the choice: if he wishes, he may hold the pawner liable, and if he wishes, he may hold the mortgagee liable, because each of them is a wrongdoer with respect to his right: the pawner by taking and delivering, and the mortgagee by receiving and keeping. If he holds the pawner liable, the mortgagee becomes a recipient of his debt through the destruction of the pawn, because the pawner owns it by paying the compensation attributed to a time before delivery, so it becomes clear that he (the pawner) owned himself (the slave) and then the mortgagee became a recipient through its destruction. And if he holds the mortgagee liable, the mortgagee recovers from the pawner the value he paid and his debt: as for the value, because he is deceived by the pawner; as for the debt, because its payment is rescinded and his right returns as it was. But if it is said: Since the ultimate liability rests on the pawner by the mortgagee's recourse against him, ownership of the compensated property is for the one upon whom the liability rests, so it becomes clear that it was the pawn of his own property, making it similar to if the claimant initially held the pawner liable. We say: This is an objection of Abu Hazim al-Qadi. The answer to it is that the mortgagee recovers from the pawner due to deception, and the deception is the mortgagee's acceptance; and the pawner owns the property from that time onward, and the pawn contract was prior to it, so it does not become clear that he pawned his own property; rather, he pawned the property of someone else. Thus the mortgagee is not a recipient by virtue of ownership of the property. And because the pawner acquires the property through receiving it from the mortgagee, as the mortgagee first owns it by paying the compensation and then it transfers to the pawner, similar to the agent for purchase, as if the buyer purchased it from the claimant. It is so because the mortgagee is a usurper with respect to the claimant. So when he pays compensation, he owns the compensated property out of necessity to avoid combining two substitutes in one ownership; then the pawner receives it from him, so his ownership is after that, and the pawn contract was prior to it, so it becomes clear that he pawned the property of another, so the mortgagee is not a recipient through the destruction, unlike the first case where the claimant initially holds the pawner liable, because he (the pawner) compensates from him based on possession prior to the pawn, so ownership is attributed to him, and it becomes clear that he pawned his own property, so the mortgagee is a recipient. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 479

Commentary
This passage is a detailed legal analysis (ta'lil) of the ruling when a pawned item dies while in the mortgagee's custody and is subsequently claimed by a third party. The author discusses two scenarios. First, if the pawner pays the value to the claimant, the pawn is considered to have expired against the debt, meaning the mortgagee's debt is satisfied. Second, if the mortgagee pays, he can recover both the value and his original debt from the pawner because the mortgagee was deceived by the pawner's delivery. The core reasoning is based on who is considered the owner at the time of destruction. If the claimant sues the pawner, ownership is traced back to before the pawn, making the pawner the owner; thus the mortgagee's debt is discharged. If the claimant sues the mortgagee, ownership passes through the mortgagee first, so the pawner's ownership is subsequent to the pawn contract, and the mortgagee is not deemed to have received satisfaction. An objection from Abu Hazim al-Qadi is answered, clarifying the distinction using the analogy of an agent buying from the true owner after a usurpation.

Key Terms
استحقاق (istihqaq): A third party's claim of ownership over the pawned item after its destruction.
غرور (ghurur): Deception that occurs when the pawner delivers the item to the mortgagee as a pawn, inducing the mortgagee to accept.
مستوفٍ (mustawfin): One who receives satisfaction of his debt; here, the mortgagee if the pawner pays the claimant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The mortgagee
B) The pawner
C) The claimant
D) The judge

Key Takeaway
When a pawned item is destroyed and claimed, the party who compensates the claimant determines whether the debt is satisfied: if pawner pays, debt is satisfied; if mortgagee pays, he recovers both value and debt from pawner.

Sale and Emancipation of the Pawn by the Pawner
Ruling that sale of pawn is suspended on mortgagee's consent; emancipation effective immediately.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the sale of a pawn by the pawner, explain the intra-Hanafi differences, and apply the correct reasoning (ta'lil) for suspension versus immediate effectiveness.

Core Idea
A pawner's sale is valid but suspended until the mortgagee consents; emancipation takes effect immediately due to its irreversible nature.

When a pawner sells the pawn without the mortgagee's permission, the sale is not automatically void. The Hanafi school reaches a nuanced position: the sale is valid in itself but suspended (mawqūf) on the mortgagee's consent or debt repayment. This lesson unpacks the conflicting statements from the classical authorities and the reasoning behind the suspension, contrasting it with the immediate effectiveness of emancipation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling in the matn
The matn states: 'The sale of the pawn is suspended on the permission of its mortgagee or the payment of his debt.' Note that 'suspended' (mawqūf) means the contract is valid but its effects are conditional.
Suspension is a third category between valid/effective (nāfidh) and void (bāṭil).
2
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Muhammad al-Shaybani gave conflicting statements: one calling the sale invalid (fāsid), another valid (jā'iz). Abu Yusuf held it effective unconditionally. The author reconciles these: the sale is valid but suspended.
The tarjih (preferred view) is that it is jā'iz mawqūf.
3
Understand the original reasoning and its critique
The original reasoning: the sale is suspended because the mortgagee's right (haqq al-habs) is attached, and executing the sale would annul it. The critic points out that the same reasoning would apply to emancipation, yet emancipation is effective. Thus the original reasoning is deficient.
The critique shows the need for a more precise illah.
4
Identify the correct illah (cause)
The proper reasoning: the sale is suspended due to the pawner's lack of ability to deliver the pawn (because it is in the mortgagee's possession and subject to his right). Emancipation does not require delivery of possession; it creates a new status that takes effect immediately.
The ability to deliver (qudra 'alā al-taslīm) is a condition for the effectiveness of contracts involving transfer of ownership, but not for freeing a slave.
5
Apply the distinction to similar dispositions
The author states that the same suspension applies to any disposition that would annul the mortgagee's right of retention, such as gift or sale. Marriage of a female slave pawn is effective because the mortgagee can still detain her from her husband.
This shows that the illah is not merely 'attachment of right' but specifically the annulment of the right of retention.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب التصرف في الرهن والجناية عليه وجنايته على غيره
لما كان التصرف في الرهن والجناية عليه وجنايته على غير متأخراً طبعاً عن كونه رهناً أخره وضعاً ليوافق الوضع الطبع . قال رحمه الله : ( ويتوقف بيع الرهن على إجازة مرتهنه أو قضاء دينه) اختلفت عبارة محمد رحمه الله تعالى في هذه المسألة ؛ قال في موضع بيع المرهون فاسد، وفي موضع جائز، والصحيح أنه جائز موقوف، وقوله فاسد محمول على إذا لم يجز المرتهن فإن القاضي يفسد إذا خوصم إليه وطلب المشتري تسليمه، وقوله جائز بمعنى محمول على ما إذا أجاز .وسلمه. وفي الجامع : باع الراهن الرهن فالبيع باطل؛ قيل معناه سيبطل، وعن أبي يوسف ينفذ سواء علم المرتهن بالبيع أو لا، وإنما يتوقف لأنه تعلق به حق المرتهن وفي بقائه إبطال حقه فلا ينفذ إلا بإجازته أو بقضاء الراهن الدين لزوال المعنى وهو تعلق حق المرتهن. أراد بالبيع ما هو مثله مما تعلق بنفاده إبطال حق المرتهن في الحبس بخلاف ما لو زوجها الراهن فإنه ينفذ ولا يتوقف على إجازة المرتهن لأن للمرتهن أن يحبسها عن الزوج كما أن للمولى ذلك. وقولهم في التعليل إنه تعلق به إلى آخره أقول : في تمام هذا التعليل من القدر نظر فإنه ينتقض بما إذا أعتق الراهن عبد الرهن ينفذ عتقه كما سيأتي في الكتاب مع جريان هذا التعليل هناك أيضاً فالوجه في التعليل ههنا أن يقال لانعدام القدرة على التسليم لتعلق حق الغير به وهو المرتهن فيتوقف على إجازته ألا ترى أن المصنف إنما فصل بين هذه المسألة ومسألة الإعتاق بانعدام القدرة على التسليم حيث قال في آخر تعليل مسألة الإعتاق من قبل أصحابنا وامتناع النفاذ في البيع والهبة لانعدام القدرة على التسليم
Chapter on Disposition of the Pawn and Tort against it, and its Tort against another.
Since the disposition of the pawn and tort against it and its tort against another are naturally posterior to its being a pawn, he (the author) deferred it structurally to match nature with structure. The author (may Allah have mercy on him) said: (The sale of the pawn is suspended on the permission of its mortgagee or the payment of his debt.) The wording of Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) differed regarding this issue: he said in one place the sale of the pawn is invalid, and in another place it is valid, and the correct view is that it is valid but suspended. His saying 'invalid' is interpreted as when the mortgagee does not permit; then the judge invalidates it if litigated and the purchaser requests delivery. His saying 'valid' is interpreted as when he (mortgagee) permits and delivers. In al-Jami': The pawner sold the pawn, so the sale is void. It is said its meaning is 'will be void.' From Abu Yusuf: It is effective whether the mortgagee knows of the sale or not. It is only suspended because the right of the mortgagee is attached to it, and upholding it (sale) would annul his right. So it does not take effect except with his permission or the pawner's payment of the debt to remove the attachment of the mortgagee's right. He intended by 'sale' what is like it among things whose execution would annul the mortgagee's right of retention, unlike the case where the pawner marries her (the slave), for that is effective and not suspended on the mortgagee's permission, because the mortgagee may detain her from the husband just as the master may. And their saying in the reasoning that it is attached etc. I say: In the completion of this reasoning there is some deficiency, because it is refuted by the case where the pawner emancipates the slave of the pawn; his emancipation takes effect as will come in the book, even though this reasoning applies there as well. So the proper reasoning here is to say: due to the lack of ability to deliver because of the attachment of another's right, namely the mortgagee's, so it is suspended on his permission. Do you not see that the author differentiated between this issue and the issue of emancipation based on lack of ability to deliver, as he said at the end of the reasoning for the emancipation issue from our scholars: 'And the prevention of effectiveness in sale and gift is due to lack of ability to deliver.'
Source pages p. 480

Commentary
This passage begins a new chapter on the pawner's dispositions of the pawn. The matn states that the sale of the pawn is suspended (muwaqqaf) upon the mortgagee's consent or the payment of the debt. The sharh explains that during Muhammad al-Shaybani's lifetime, various expressions were used—some calling it invalid, some valid—and the correct interpretation is that it is valid but suspended. The hanafi jurist Abu Yusuf even held it effective unconditionally. The reason for suspension is that the mortgagee has a right of retention (haqq al-habs) attached to the pawn. Executing a sale would annul that right, so it cannot be effective without the mortgagee's permission or the debt's payment. In contrast, marriage of a female slave pawn is effective immediately because the mortgagee can still detain her from her husband. They also discuss the difference between sale and emancipation: emancipation is effective despite the mortgagee's right because it brings about a new status that cannot be undone, and the mortgagee's right continues in the form of detention of the free person for the debt. The proper reasoning for suspension in sale is the lack of ability to deliver subject to another's right.

Key Terms
موقوف (mawqūf): A legal act that is valid but its effectiveness is suspended upon occurrence of a condition (here, mortgagee's permission or debt payment).
حق الحبس (haqq al-habs): The mortgagee's right to retain possession of the pawn until the debt is paid.
القدرة على التسليم (al-qudra 'alā al-taslīm): Ability to deliver possession of a sold item to the buyer; a condition for the effectiveness of a sale contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the status of a sale of a pawn by the pawner without the mortgagee's permission?
A) Void (bāṭil)
B) Valid and effective immediately
C) Valid but suspended (mawqūf)
D) Valid only if the mortgagee is informed

Key Takeaway
A pawner's sale is valid but suspended on the mortgagee's consent due to lack of ability to deliver, while emancipation is effective immediately because it creates an irreversible status of freedom.

Distinction Between Sale and Emancipation of Pawn
Explains why emancipation of pawn is effective unlike sale.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that the emancipation of a pawn is effective immediately while sale is suspended on the mortgagee's permission.

Core Idea
Emancipation requires no delivery; sale requires delivery—so the mortgagee's control blocks sale but not emancipation.

In this passage, the Hanafi jurists refine a critical distinction. Both sale and emancipation are acts of disposal over a pawned item, yet they are treated differently. The reason lies in a condition unique to sales: ability to deliver. This lesson unpacks that reasoning and addresses the Shafi'i objection.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two transactions compared
Recognize that the passage contrasts sale (and gift) with emancipation of a pawn. Both involve disposal of the pawned property, yet the ruling differs.
Sale and gift are grouped together as requiring delivery.
2
State the Hanafi ruling for each
Emancipation is effective immediately (nafidh) without permission. Sale and gift are suspended (mawquf) on the mortgagee's permission or debt payment.
3
Locate the distinguishing factor
The passage states that sale lacks effect due to the absence of ability to deliver (al-qudrah 'ala al-taslim). The mortgagee's hand (control) prevents delivery. Emancipation does not require delivery.
Delivery is a condition for the validity of sale in the Hanafi school.
4
Understand the mechanism of permission
If the mortgagee permits the sale, his right transfers to the price, so the price becomes the new pawn. Thus delivery becomes possible.
Permission removes the impediment by shifting the security to the price.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Shafi'is argue that emancipation should also be suspended since it diminishes the pawn. Hanafis respond that emancipation does not require delivery, so the mortgagee's possession is not an obstacle.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different emphasis on the condition of delivery.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لما كان التصرف في الرهن والجناية عليه وجنايته على غير متأخراً طبعاً عن كونه رهناً أخره وضعاً ليوافق الوضع الطبع . قال رحمه الله : ( ويتوقف بيع الرهن على إجازة مرتهنه أو قضاء دينه) ... وامتناع النفاذ بالبيع والهبة لانعدام القدرة على التسليم لأن يد المرتهن مانعة عن التسليم والبيع كما يفتقر إلى الملك يفتقر إلى القدر لا على التسليم فإذا انعقد البيع بإجازة المرتهن انتقل حقه إلى الثمن فيكون محبوساً بالدين.
Since disposal of the pawn, injuries upon it, and its injury to others are naturally subsequent to its being a pawn, it was placed later in the text to match the natural order. He (the author) said: 'The sale of a pawn is suspended on the permission of its mortgagee or the payment of his debt.' ... And the lack of effect in sale and gift is due to the absence of ability to deliver because the hand of the mortgagee prevents delivery. Sale, just as it requires ownership, requires ability to deliver. If the sale is concluded with the mortgagee's permission, his right transfers to the price, so it becomes detained for the debt.
Source pages p. 480

Commentary
This passage refines the reasoning for why emancipation is effective but sale is not. The key factor is the ability to deliver. Emancipation does not require delivery; it is a mere declaration that does not involve physical transfer. Sale, however, requires the seller to deliver the item to the buyer. Since the mortgagee's hand (control) prevents the pledgor from delivering, the sale cannot be effective without the mortgagee's permission, which removes his hand by transferring his right to the price. This distinction answers the objection: why doesn't the same suspension apply to emancipation? Because emancipation does not require delivery.

Key Terms
القدرة على التسليم (al-qudrah 'ala al-taslim): The legal ability to physically deliver the sold item to the buyer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Emancipation is an act of worship and thus must be valid.
B) Emancipation does not require physical delivery of the slave.
C) The mortgagee's permission is automatically given for emancipation.
D) The pawn is not fully owned by the pledgor.

Key Takeaway
The distinction hinges on the condition of ability to deliver: sale requires it, emancipation does not.

Does the Price Become Pawned Automatically?
Dispute between Abu Yusuf and zahir al-riwayah on status of price.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position (zahir al-riwayah) on automatic transfer of the price when the mortgagee permits the sale of a pawn, and explain the distinction from the lease scenario.

Core Idea
The price of a sold pawn automatically becomes pawned because it replaces the original pawn — a substitute inherits the ruling of the original.

When a mortgagee permits the sale of a pawn, does the price automatically become a new pawn in place of the original? This dispute between Abu Yusuf and the authoritative narration (zahir al-riwayah) hinges on whether the price is a mere new acquisition or a true substitute. The correct view, relying on the well-established principle that a substitute takes the ruling of the substituted thing, affirms automatic transfer. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The core legal question: when the mortgagee permits the sale, does the price become automatically pawned in place of the original pawn?
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf vs. zahir al-riwayah.
2
State Abu Yusuf's view and proof
Abu Yusuf argues that the price does not become pawned unless stipulated. His proof: the pledgor acquires the price by a new cause (sale), analogous to lease where rent does not become pawned automatically.
He relies on the new cause (sabab jadid) to sever the connection.
3
State the position of zahir al-riwayah
The authoritative tradition holds that the price does become pawned automatically. The proof: the price is the substitute (badal) of the original pawn; a substitute has the same legal status as the original. This is supported by the case of a debtor slave sold with consent of creditors — their right transfers to the price.
The rule: al-badlu lahu hukm al-mubaddal.
4
Distinguish the lease analogy
The Hanafi response distinguishes lease: rent is not a substitute for the pawn itself; it is a new obligation arising from a separate contract. Therefore, the automatic transfer rule does not apply to rent.
The right in the pawn is attached to the physical pawn; rent is not a substitute for that right.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The view of zahir al-riwayah is correct and is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi). This means in practice, the price becomes pawned automatically unless the mortgagee explicitly stipulates otherwise.
Practical consequence: the mortgagee can detain the price until the debt is paid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعن أبي يوسف رحمه الله تعالى أن المرتهن إن شرط أن يكون الثمن رهناً عند الإجازة كان رهناً وإلا فلا فلأنه بالإجازة نفذ البيع وملك الراهن الثمن وأن ماله أخذه فملكه بسبب جديد فلا تصير رهناً إلا بالشرط كما إذا أجره الراهن فأجازة المرتهن الإجارة لا تصير الأجرة رهناً إلا بالشرط. وجه ظاهر الرواية وهو الصحيح أن الثمن قائم مقام ما يتعلق به حقه وهو بدل ما تعلق به حقه ومحل لحقه لأن حقه تعلق بماله وللبدل حكم المبدل فوجب انتقال حقه إليه كالعبد المديون إذا بيع برضا الغرماء ينتقل حقهم إلى البدل من غير شرط لما ذكرنا ولا يسقط حقهم بالكلية لعدم رضاهم بذلك ظاهراً والرضا بالبيع لا يدل على الرضا لسقوط الحق رأساً فيبقى الحق على غيره بخلاف ما ذكر لأن الأجرة ليست ببدل حقه، وبخلاف ما إذا باع العين المستأجرة فأجاز المستأجر البيع حيث لا ينقل حقه إلى الثمن لأنه ليس ببدل العين وحقه في العين فافترقا.
And it is narrated from Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him) that if the mortgagee stipulates that the price be a pawn at the time of permission, then it becomes a pawn; otherwise, no. Because by the permission the sale becomes effective and the pledgor owns the price, and he takes it, so he owns it by a new cause, so it does not become a pawn except by stipulation, just as if the pledgor leases (the pawn) and the mortgagee permits the lease, the rent does not become a pawn except by stipulation. The view of the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah), which is correct, is that the price stands in place of what his right was attached to; it is the substitute of what his right was attached to and the locus of his right, because his right was attached to the commodity, and a substitute has the same rule as the substituted thing, so his right must transfer to it, like the case of a slave who is in debt: if he is sold with the consent of the creditors, their right transfers to the price without stipulation, for the reason we mentioned, and their right is not completely dropped because they did not explicitly consent to dropping it; rather, consent to the sale does not indicate consent to dropping the right entirely, so the right remains on something else. This differs from what was mentioned because the rent is not a substitute for his right, and also differs from the case where a leased item is sold and the lessee permits the sale, where his right does not transfer to the price because the price is not a substitute for the item and his right is in the item itself, so they are different.
Source pages p. 480

Commentary
This passage addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute: when the mortgagee permits the sale, does the price become automatically pawned in place of the original pawn? Abu Yusuf says no, it remains free unless the mortgagee stipulates it as a pawn. The reason is that the pledgor acquires the price by a new cause, independent of the original pawn. However, the view of the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) — which is correct — is that the price automatically becomes pawned because it is the substitute of the original pawn. The mortgagee's right attaches to the substitute just as in the case of a debtor slave sold with creditors' consent. The distinction with rent from lease is that rent is not a substitute for the pawn itself, so it does not become pawned automatically. The correct view (zahir al-riwayah) is the relied-upon position.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The transmitted rulings from the six core books of Imam Muhammad, considered the most authoritative.
بدل (badal): Substitute; the price that replaces the pawn.
إجازة (ijazah): Permission; here, the mortgagee's consent to the sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct Hanafi position (zahir al-riwayah), when the mortgagee permits the sale of the pawn, the price:
A) Becomes pawned only if the mortgagee stipulates
B) Becomes pawned automatically
C) Remains free always
D) Becomes property of the mortgagee

Key Takeaway
The price of a sold pawn automatically becomes pawned when the mortgagee permits, because the price is the substitute of the pawn and inherits its legal status.

Effect of Mortgagee's Rescission and Multiple Sales
Rulings on mortgagee's rejection of sale and multiple sales of pawn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the mortgagee's rescission of a pawn sale and apply the rule for multiple sales to determine which contract becomes binding.

Core Idea
The mortgagee cannot unilaterally rescind a pawn sale; only the judge can; multiple sales are suspended until his permission.

When a pawned property is sold by the pledgor, the mortgagee may refuse to permit the sale. Two narrations from Imam Muhammad exist on whether the mortgagee's rescission itself voids the sale. The more authentic view holds that the sale remains suspended, not rescinded. This lesson unpacks that ruling, the buyer's options, and the rules when the same pawn is sold to multiple buyers or followed by other contracts like lease or gift.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two narrations
Recognize that Ibn Samā‘a narrated from Muhammad that the mortgagee's rescission rescinds the sale, but the more authentic view (sahih al-riwayatayn) is that it does not. The Mukhtasar indicates that the sale is only suspended pending permission or debt payment.
The more authentic view protects the mortgagee's right of detention from being nullified.
2
Understand the buyer's options
The buyer may wait for the pledgor to redeem the pawn or refer the matter to the judge. The judge can rescind the contract due to inability to deliver, as the authority to rescind belongs only to the judge.
Analogy: a sold slave who runs away before delivery — the buyer has similar options.
3
Apply the rule to multiple sales
If the pledgor sells the same pawn to two different buyers before the mortgagee permits, both sales are suspended. Whichever sale the mortgagee permits becomes binding, and the other is void. A suspended contract does not prevent the suspension of another.
The mortgagee's permission determines which sale takes effect based on benefit.
4
Distinguish beneficial and non-beneficial subsequent contracts
If the mortgagee permits a later lease, pawn, or gift instead of the earlier sale, the earlier sale becomes effective and the later contracts are void. The mortgagee only benefits from the sale because his right transfers to the price, not from other contracts.
This ensures the mortgagee's interest is protected.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن لم يجز المرتهن البيع وفسخه انفسخ في رواية ابن سماعة عن محمد حتى إذا أفتكه الراهن لا سبيل للمشتري عليه لأن الحق الثابت للمرتهن بمنزلة الملك فصار كالمالك فله أن يجيز وله أن يفسخ، وفي أصح الروايتين لا ينفسخ بفسخه. وفي المختصر إشارة إليه حيث قال: توقف على إجازة المرتهن أو قضاء دينه جعل الإجارة إليه دون الفسخ وجعله متوقفاً على قضاء الدين، وهذا دليل على أن فسخه لا ينفذ ووجه الامتناع لحقه كيلا يتضرر والتوقف لا يضره لأن حقه في الحبس لا يبطل بمجرد الانعقاد من غير نفوذ فبقي متوقفاً على المشتري، ثم إن المشتري بالخيار إن شاء صبر حتى يفتك الراهن الرهن إذ العجز على شرف الزوال، وإن شاء رفع الأمر إلى القاضي وللقاضي أن يفسخ العقد لفوات القدرة على التسليم لأن ولاية الفسخ له لا إلى المشتري والبائع وهو الراهن وصار كالعبد المبيع إذا أبق قبل القبض فإن المشتري بالخيار إن شاء صبر حتى يرجع، وإن شاء رفع الأمر إلى القاضي والإجارة مثل الرهن حتى لا ينفذ بيع المؤجر، ولو باعه الراهن من رجل ثم باعه من آخر قبل أن يجيز المرتهن فالثاني موقوف أيضاً على إجازته لأن الأول لم ينفذ والموقوف لا يمنع توقف الثاني فأيهما أجاز لزم ذلك وبطل الآخر. ولو باعه الراهن ثم أجره أو رهنه أو وهبه من غيره فأجاز المرتهن الإجارة أو الرهن أو الهبة جاز البيع الأول دون هذه العقود. والفرق أن المرتهن له منفعة في البيع لأن حقه يتحول إلى الثمن على ما بينا وقد يكون أحد العقدين أنفع من الآخر فيعتبر تعيينه لتعلق الفائدة أما هذه العقود فلا منفعة له فيها لأن حقه لا ينقل إلى الآخر لما بينا.
If the mortgagee does not permit the sale and rescinds it, then it is rescinded according to the narration of Ibn Samā‘a from Muḥammad, such that if the pledgor later redeems the pawn, the buyer has no recourse against him, because the right established for the mortgagee is like ownership, so he becomes like the owner; he may permit and he may rescind. But in the more authentic of the two narrations, it is not rescinded by his rescission. In al-Mukhtaṣar there is an indication of this, where he said: 'It is suspended on the permission of the mortgagee or the payment of his debt' — he made permission a cause for effect but not rescission, and he made it suspended on debt payment. This is evidence that his rescission is not effective. The reason for its lack of effect is to avoid harm to him (the mortgagee), and suspension does not harm him because his right of detention is not nullified by the mere conclusion of the sale without effect; it remains suspended for the buyer. Then the buyer has a choice: if he wishes, he may wait until the pledgor redeems the pawn, because the inability (to deliver) is about to end; and if he wishes, he may refer the matter to the judge, and the judge may rescind the contract due to loss of ability to deliver, because the authority of rescission belongs to him (the judge), not to the buyer or the seller (the pledgor). This is like the case of a sold slave who runs away before delivery: the buyer has a choice to wait or refer to the judge. And lease is like pawn in that the sale by the lessor is not effective. If the pledgor sells the pawn to one man and then sells it to another before the mortgagee permits, the second sale is also suspended on his permission because the first did not take effect, and a suspended contract does not prevent the suspension of another. Whichever (sale) the mortgagee permits becomes binding and the other is void. If the pledgor sells it and then leases it, pawns it, or gifts it to another, and the mortgagee permits the lease, pawn, or gift, then the first (sale) is valid and these later contracts are not valid. The difference is that the mortgagee has benefit in the sale because his right transfers to the price, as we explained, and one of the two contracts might be more beneficial to him, so his specification (of which to permit) is considered because of the benefit attached. As for these (other) contracts, he has no benefit in them because his right does not transfer to another (consideration), as we explained.
Source pages p. 481

Commentary
This passage covers several rules after the mortgagee's refusal to permit. There are two narrations from Muhammad: one says the mortgagee's rescission rescinds the sale (Ibn Samā‘a), but the more authentic view is that his rescission does not rescind. The sale remains suspended. The buyer then has options: wait for redemption or go to the judge who can rescind due to inability to deliver. This is analogous to a slave that runs away before delivery. Additionally, if the pledgor sells the same pawn to two different buyers before the mortgagee permits, both sales are suspended. Whichever the mortgagee permits becomes binding. If the mortgagee permits a subsequent lease, pawn, or gift instead of the earlier sale, the earlier sale becomes effective and the later contracts are void, because the mortgagee only benefits from the sale (since his right transfers to the price), not from those other contracts.

Key Terms
فسخ (faskh): Rescission of a contract by one party or the judge. In this context, the mortgagee's rescission is not effective.
موقوف (mawquf): Suspended; a contract whose validity depends on a future condition (here, the mortgagee's permission).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Both sales are void.
B) The first sale is valid, the second is void.
C) Both sales are suspended; whichever the mortgagee permits becomes binding.
D) The second sale is valid because the first is suspended.

Key Takeaway
The mortgagee's rescission does not rescind the pawn sale; the sale remains suspended, and for multiple sales, the mortgagee's permission determines which becomes binding.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Transfer of Mortgagee's Right to the Price
Intra-Hanafi dispute on automatic transfer of mortgagee's right to price

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the relied-upon Hanafi position that the mortgagee's right automatically transfers to the price, and distinguish it from Abu Yusuf's view requiring stipulation, by analysing the underlying qiyas and its distinction from analogous cases.

Core Idea
The price stands in place of the collateral; the substitute takes the ruling of the substituted.

When a mortgagor sells the collateral with the mortgagee's permission, what happens to the mortgagee's security? Does his right automatically attach to the price, or does he lose it unless he stipulates? This lesson unpacks an intra-Hanafi dispute on this very question, focusing on the relied-upon view from Zahir al-Riwayah and how it distinguishes between sale and lease scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Issue
Determine the exact legal question: when the mortgagor sells the collateral with the mortgagee's permission, does the mortgagee's right transfer to the price automatically or only if stipulated?
The answer affects whether the debt remains secured after the sale.
2
Contrast the Two Positions
The relied-upon view (Zahir al-Riwayah) holds automatic transfer. Abu Yusuf holds that transfer requires stipulation. Note each side's key argument.
The disagreement is about the nature of the permission and the status of the substitute.
3
Analyse the Hanafi Proof for Automatic Transfer
Understand the qiyas: the price is a substitute (badal) for the collateral; the substitute inherits the ruling of the substituted, exactly as in the case of an indebted slave sold with creditors' consent. The effective cause is that the substitute directly replaces the property to which the right was attached.
The consent to sell does not imply consent to drop the right entirely.
4
Examine Abu Yusuf's Counter-Analogy
Abu Yusuf analogises to a lease: if the mortgagor leases the collateral with the mortgagee's permission, the rent does not become collateral unless stipulated. He argues that permission perfects a new ownership cause for the price, so it does not automatically attach.
The relied-upon view distinguishes: rent is a substitute for usufruct, not for the property itself.
5
Apply the Distinction to Concrete Cases
Test the reasoning: under which view is the debt secured if the price is wasted? The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is whether the mortgagee can still claim the price from the mortgagor's hands as collateral.
The mufta bihi view ensures the debt remains secured automatically.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الرهن باب التصرف في الرهن والجناية عليه وجنايته على غيره فتدبر قوله وامتناع النفاذ بالبيع والهبة لانعدام القدرة على التسليم لأن يد المرتهن مانعة عن التسليم والبيع كما يفتقر إلى الملك يفتقر إلى القدرة على التسليم فإذا انعقد البيع بإجازة المرتهن انتقل حقه إلى الثمن فيكون محبوساً بالدين. وعن أبي يوسف رحمه الله تعالى أن المرتهن إن شرط أن يكون الثمن رهناً عند الإجازة كان رهناً وإلا فلا فلأنه بالإجازة نفذ البيع وملك الراهن الثمن وأن ماله أخذه فملكه بسبب جديد فلا تصير رهناً إلا بالشرط كما إذا أجره الراهن فأجازة المرتهن الإجارة لا تصير الأجرة رهناً إلا بالشرط. وجه ظاهر الرواية وهو الصحيح أن الثمن قائم مقام ما يتعلق به حقه وهو بدل ما تعلق به حقه ومحل لحقه لأن حقه تعلق بماله وللبدل حكم المبدل فوجب انتقال حقه إليه كالعبد المديون إذا بيع برضا الغرماء ينتقل حقهم إلى البدل من غير شرط لما ذكرنا ولا يسقط حقهم بالكلية لعدم رضاهم بذلك ظاهراً والرضا بالبيع لا يدل على الرضا لسقوط الحق رأساً فيبقى الحق على غيره بخلاف ما ذكر لأن الأجرة ليست ببدل حقه، وبخلاف ما إذا باع العين المستأجرة فأجاز المستأجر البيع حيث لا ينقل حقه إلى الثمن لأنه ليس ببدل العين وحقه في العين فافترقا،
Book of Mortgage: Chapter on Disposition in the Mortgage and Injury upon It and Its Injury upon Others. So ponder his statement: 'And prohibition of effectiveness through sale and gift due to lack of ability to deliver because the hand of the mortgagee prevents delivery. And sale, just as it requires ownership, it requires ability to deliver. So when the sale is concluded with the mortgagee's permission, his right transfers to the price, so it becomes held as collateral for the debt.' And from Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, that the mortgagee, if he stipulates that the price be collateral at the time of permission, it is collateral; otherwise not, because with permission the sale becomes effective and the mortgagor owns the price, and his property has taken it, so he owns it by a new cause; thus it does not become collateral except by stipulation, just as if the mortgagor leases it and the mortgagee permits the lease, the rent does not become collateral except by stipulation. The apparent transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah) and it is the correct one: that the price stands in place of what his right is attached to, and it is a substitute for what his right is attached to, and a locus for his right, because his right is attached to his property, and the substitute has the ruling of the substituted, so his right must transfer to it, like the indebted slave when sold with the consent of the creditors: their right transfers to the substitute without stipulation, due to what we have mentioned, and their right does not drop entirely because their apparent consent to the sale does not indicate consent to dropping the right entirely; thus the right remains on others. Unlike what was mentioned because the rent is not a substitute for his right, and unlike when the leased property is sold and the lessee permits the sale, where his right does not transfer to the price because it is not a substitute for the property and his right is in the property, so they differ.
Source pages p. 481

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq deals with the ruling on the sale of mortgaged property. The author states that a sale by the mortgagor without the mortgagee's permission is suspended (mawquf) because the mortgagee's right prevents delivery. When the mortgagee permits the sale, the mortgagor's ownership is perfected and the mortgagee's right transfers from the collateral to its price, so the price becomes held as collateral for the debt. Then an intra-Hanafi dispute is presented: According to Abu Yusuf, the price becomes collateral only if the mortgagee stipulates that condition at the time of permission; otherwise it does not. His reasoning is that the permission causes the sale to become effective and the mortgagor becomes owner of the price by a new cause, so it does not automatically become collateral. He analogizes to a lease: if the mortgagor leases the collateral and the mortgagee permits it, the rent does not become collateral unless stipulated. The relied-upon position (Zahir al-Riwayah), which is correct, holds that the price automatically becomes collateral without stipulation. The proof is that the price stands in place of the collateral; it is a substitute for what the right was attached to. Since the right was attached to the property, and the substitute takes the ruling of the substituted, the right transfers to the price. This is analogous to the case of a slave who is indebted: when the slave is sold with the consent of the creditors, their right transfers to the substitute without stipulation, as their consent to the sale does not imply consent to dropping the right entirely. The author then distinguishes the lease case: rent is not a substitute for the property itself, and the lessee's right is in the property itself, not in a substitute. Therefore, the mortgagee's right does not transfer when the mortgagor grants a lease and the mortgagee permits it.

Key Terms
رهن (rahn): The property given as security for a debt; collateral.
مرتهن (murtahin): The creditor who holds the collateral; the mortgagee.
بدل (badal): A substitute, specifically the price (thaman) that replaces the collateral in the mortgagee's right.
إجازة (ijaza): Permission or consent given by the mortgagee to the mortgagor to dispose of the collateral.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon Hanafi position regarding the mortgagee's right when the mortgagor sells the collateral with permission?
A) The mortgagee's right is extinguished because he consented to the sale.
B) The mortgagee's right transfers to the price automatically.
C) The mortgagee must stipulate that the price becomes collateral; otherwise it does not.
D) The mortgagee retains the right to reclaim the collateral from the buyer.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, when a mortgagor sells the collateral with the mortgagee's permission, the mortgagee's right automatically transfers to the price, securing the debt without the need for stipulation.

Pledgor's Freeing of Pawned Slave: Effective but Compensated
States ruling and proof for effective freeing, rebuts objection, and details intra-Hanafi dispute on compensation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the pledgor freeing a pawned slave, explain the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and apply the ruling to analogous cases.

Core Idea
Ownership overrides possession: freeing is effective, but mortgagee's right is compensated.

This passage addresses a classic question in pawn (rahn): can the pledgor free a pawned slave? The ruling is that the freeing is legally effective (nāfidh), contrary to a view that it is suspended. However, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute on how the mortgagee's right is protected. By analysing the arguments, you will understand the Hanafi principle that ownership is stronger than mere possession, and that a valid disposition is not void even if it affects a security interest.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the pledgor (owner) freeing a slave that is currently pawned as collateral. The ruling stated is that the freeing is effective (nāfidh) – it takes effect immediately and is valid.
The text opens with 'wa nafadha 'itquhu' – his freeing is effective.
2
Understand the Hanafi proof
The proof is by analogy (qiyas) to cases where ownership overrides a lesser right: a seller freeing a slave before delivery, freeing a runaway slave, or freeing a jointly-owned slave. In each, the owner's disposition is valid despite another's interest, because ownership (milk al-raqaba) is stronger than possession (yad). The mortgagee only has a security interest, not ownership.
The passage says 'li-anna milk al-raqaba aqwā min al-yad'.
3
Recognize the intra-Hanafi dispute
While all Hanafi authorities agree the freeing is effective, they differ on compensation. Abu Hanifa holds that the slave must work (sa'yah) to pay off the debt, delaying full freedom. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) hold that the slave is freed immediately and the value becomes the new pawn, protecting the mortgagee's right.
The text mentions 'ind al-Imām yu'akhkhir ilā adā' al-sa'āyah' vs. 'yattaqi al-thānī wa al-thālith fī al-hāl'.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah)
Under Abu Hanifa, the slave remains in pawn until the debt is paid through earnings. Under the Sahibayn, the slave is freed at once and the value serves as the pawn. The later fatwa generally follows the Sahibayn for greater protection of the mortgagee.
The muftā bihī is the view of the Sahibayn (immediate freeing and replacement).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ونفذ عتقه) أي نفذ عتق الراهن وهو قول الشافعي رحمه الله تعالى وفي قول آخر لا ينفذ موسراً كان أو معسراً لأن في تنفيذه إبطال حق المرتهن. ولنا أن العتق صدر أهله مضافاً إلى محله ملکه ووجب بنفاذه ولا يلغو تصرفه لعدم إذن المرتهن كما إذا أعتق المبيع قبل القبض أو الآبق أو المغصوب، وإذا زال ملك الراهن عن رقبته بإعتاقه بزول ملك المرتهن لأنه بناء عليه كإعتاق العبد المشترك بل أولى لأن ملك الرقبة أقوى من اليد، فإذا لم يمتنع الأعلى فالأدنى أولى أن لا يمنعه، ولا يلزمنا إعتاق الوارث العبد الموصي برقبته إذا لم يكن له مال آخر حيث إنه لا ينفذ مع أنه أعتق ملكه لأنا نقول : يعتق عند الثاني والثالث في الحال. وعند الإمام يؤخر إلى أداء السعاية على ما عرف في إعتاق العبد المشترك ولم يكن إعتاقه لغواً وهو ههنا جعله لغواً. ولا يقال المرهون كالخارج عن ملك الراهن بدليل أن المولى إذا أتلفه يجب عليه ضمانه فكذا لا ينفذ عتقه لأنه خرج عن ملكه لأنا نقول : الضمان عليه باعتبار أنه إذا أتلف المالية المشغولة بحق المرتهن كالمولى يتلف عبده المأذون له فإنه يضمن قيمته للغرماء مع بقاء ملكه فيه من كل وجه، ولهذا ينفذ تصرفه فيه.
He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: (And his freeing is effective) meaning the freeing of the pledgor is effective, and this is the saying of al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him). In another saying, it is not effective, whether he is wealthy or insolvent, because implementing it would nullify the mortgagee's right. But we argue: the freeing came from its rightful person, directed to its place, his property, and it is obligatory to enforce it; his disposition is not invalidated due to lack of permission from the mortgagee, just like if he sells the sold item before delivery, or a runaway slave, or a usurped slave. And when the pledgor's ownership of the slave's person is removed by his freeing, the mortgagee's ownership (right) is removed because it is built upon it, like freeing a jointly owned slave—indeed more so, because ownership of the person is stronger than possession. So if the stronger does not prevent, the weaker is more deserving of not preventing. And we are not bound by the case of the heir freeing a slave whose usufruct was bequeathed when he has no other property, where it is not effective even though he freed his property; because we say: it takes effect immediately according to the second and third (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). According to the Imam (Abu Hanifa), it is delayed until the payment of earnings, as known in freeing a jointly owned slave, and his freeing was not void, whereas here he made it void. And it should not be said: the pawn is like outside the pledgor's ownership, evidenced by the fact that if the master destroys it, he must guarantee it, so likewise his freeing is not effective because it has left his ownership; because we say: the guarantee is upon him because he destroyed the financial value encumbered with the mortgagee's right, like a master destroying his slave who is permitted (to trade) – he guarantees its value to the creditors while his ownership remains in him in every respect, and therefore his disposition is valid in it.
Source pages p. 484

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effectiveness of a pledgor freeing a pawned slave. The text opens by stating the ruling that the freeing is effective (nāfidh), attributing it to Imam al-Shafi'i, but then notes there is another opinion that it is not effective. The Hanafi position presented here is that it is effective, as articulated by Abu Hanifa. The proof is rational: the pledgor is the owner, the act of freeing is validly performed, and the mortgagee's right is merely a security interest, not ownership. The commentator compares it to other cases where ownership overrides possession, such as selling a slave before delivery. He also addresses the objection that the pawn is like being outside ownership by analogy to destruction: the guarantee is for the financial value encumbered, not for the slave's person, so ownership remains. The response includes the well-known ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa (who defers freeing until the slave pays off the debt via sa'yah) and the two disciples (who free immediately and take the value as pawn). The commentator defends Abu Hanifa's view by analogy to the jointly owned slave. The key takeaway is that the freeing is not void; rather, the slave is liable for compensation.

Key Terms
نَافِذ (nāfidh): A disposition that is legally effective and takes immediate effect, not suspended.
سَعَايَة (sa‘āyah): The earnings a slave acquires by working to pay off a debt or obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens to a pawned slave when the pledgor frees him and the pledgor is insolvent?
A) The freeing is void and the slave remains pawned.
B) The slave is freed immediately and the value becomes a pawn.
C) The slave must work to pay the debt (sa'yah) according to Abu Hanifa.
D) The mortgagee loses his right entirely.

Key Takeaway
A pledgor's freeing of a pawned slave is effective, but the mortgagee's right must be compensated; the Hanafi school differs on the method of compensation.

Extension of Freeing to Tadbeer and Istilad in Rahn
Extends ruling of freeing to tadbeer and istilad with al-Mabsut quotation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on tadbeer and istilad of a pawned slave and apply the compensation rules based on the pledgor's solvency.

Core Idea
Tadbeer and istilad of a pawned slave are effective; compensation is ensured through substitution or istis'a.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq critiques the original matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq for not explicitly including tadbeer. The commentator argues that since tadbeer is weaker than istilad, and both freeing and istilad are effective, tadbeer is effective by an a fortiori argument (min bab awla). He then cites al-Mabsut to demonstrate that the three dispositions—freeing, tadbeer, and istilad—are all effective, with specific compensation mechanisms depending on the pledgor's solvency.

Guided Path
1
Identify the extension
The commentator suggests the author should have included 'tadbeer' alongside 'freeing'. Recognize that the ruling is being extended by qiyas awla.
Tadbeer is a weaker form of manumission than istilad.
2
Analyze the a fortiori argument
If a stronger disposition (freeing/istilad) is effective, then a weaker one (tadbeer) is effective by greater reason. Understand the logic: min bab awla.
This is a form of qiyas jali.
3
Understand the compensation from al-Mabsut
If the pledgor is solvent, he must pay the value as substitute. If insolvent, he can require the mudabbar/umm walad to earn (istis'a') for the entire debt, and the freed slave for his value.
The mortgagee's right is preserved through value or earnings.
4
Distinguish solvent vs insolvent
Note the two scenarios: musir (wealthy) vs mu'sir (insolvent). The compensation method differs.
Insolvency means the pledgor cannot pay immediately.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قال المؤلف ونفذ تدبيره لكان أولى إذا علم نفاذ التدبير من الراهن والتدبير أدنى حالاً من الاستيلاد علم نفاذ الاستيلاء والإعتاق من باب أولى قال في المبسوط : إعتاق الراهن وتدبيره واستيلاده ينفذ ويضمن القيمة ويكون رهناً مكانه إن كان موسراً، ثم إن كان المال حالاً اقتضاه من القيمة، وإن كان الراهن معسراً فللراهن استسعاء المدبر وأم الولد في جميع الدين والمعتق في قيمته ثم يرجع المعتق بما أدى على المولى.
And if the author had said 'and his tadbeer is effective' it would have been better, since it is known that tadbeer from the pledgor is effective. And tadbeer is inferior in status to istilad, so it is known that istilad and freeing are effective by even greater reason. He said in al-Mabsut: The pledgor's freeing, tadbeer, and istilad are effective, and he guarantees the value, and it becomes a pawn in its place if he is wealthy. Then if the debt is due, he collects from the value. If the pledgor is insolvent, then the pledgor may seek earnings (istis'ā') from the mudabbar and the umm walad for the entire debt, and from the freed slave for his value. Then the latter (the freed one) will have recourse to the master for what he paid.
Source pages p. 484

Commentary
This passage is a note by the commentator suggesting that the author should have included 'tadbeer' (making a slave mudabbar) alongside 'freeing' in the ruling. The reasoning is that tadbeer is a weaker form of manumission than istilad (making a slave umm walad), so if the stronger (istilad and freeing) is effective, the weaker (tadbeer) is effective by greater reason (min bāb awlā). The commentator then quotes from al-Mabsut: all three dispositions (freeing, tadbeer, istilad) are effective. If the pledgor is solvent, he must pay the value of the slave as a replacement pawn. If the debt is due, the mortgagee takes from that value. If insolvent, the pledgor can require the mudabbar and umm walad to earn for the entire debt, and the freed slave to earn for his value; then the freed slave can claim reimbursement from the master. This shows the Hanafi position that the mortgagee's right is preserved through substitution of value or sa'yah.

Key Terms
تَدْبِير (tadbeer): Declaration that a slave will be free upon the master's death.
اِسْتِيلاد (istilad): A female slave becoming umm walad by bearing her master's child.
إِسْتِسْعَاء (istis'a'): Requiring a slave to earn money to pay off a debt or value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The pledgor can keep the mudabbar without any obligation.
B) The pledgor can require the mudabbar to earn for the entire debt.
C) The mudabbar is immediately freed and no compensation is needed.
D) The mortgagee must release the pawn.

Key Takeaway
Tadbeer and istilad of a pawned slave are effective; compensation through value substitution or istis'a preserves the mortgagee's rights.
