Rulings when a Pawned Slave is Freed by the Pledgor
States three rulings for mortgagee when pledged slave is freed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi rulings when a pawned slave is freed by the pledgor: for a due debt, a deferred debt, and an insolvent pledgor, and explain the calculation of sa'yah according to al-Jami'.

Core Idea
A freed pawned slave compensates the mortgagee only for the lesser of his value, the guaranteed amount, or the detained amount.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq, with commentary from al-Bahr al-Raiq, outlines the Hanafi rules when a pledgor frees a pawned slave. The mortgagee's rights depend on whether the debt is due or deferred and whether the pledgor is solvent or insolvent. These rules balance the slave's freedom with the mortgagee's security interest.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
The passage covers three cases: (1) debt due and pledgor solvent, (2) debt deferred and pledgor solvent, (3) pledgor insolvent. For each, the mortgagee's recourse differs.
Solvency of the pledgor is key—determines whether the mortgagee can demand payment from the pledgor or must seek compensation from the slave.
2
State the ruling for due debt (solvent pledgor)
If the debt is due, the mortgagee can demand the debt from the pledgor directly. Taking the slave as pawn would be pointless if the debt is of the same type (it would be self-payment).
The ruling avoids an unnecessary transfer of the pawn.
3
State the ruling for deferred debt (solvent pledgor)
If the debt is deferred, the mortgagee takes the value of the freed slave and holds it as a replacement pawn until the term expires. This maintains security without forcing early payment.
The value is determined at the time of freeing.
4
State the ruling for insolvent pledgor
If the pledgor is insolvent, the freed slave must work (sa'yah) to compensate the mortgagee. The amount is the lesser of the slave's value or the debt according to the author, but al-Jami' specifies the lesser of three: value, amount guaranteed by the debt, and amount for which he was detained.
The 'lesser of three' rule prevents the slave from paying more than the actual loss to the mortgagee.
5
Apply the lesser-of-three rule to examples
Work through the examples: (a) Slave worth 1000, debt 1000, pledgor pays 900, then frees while insolvent → slave works for 100 (debt remaining). (b) Slave worth 1000, debt 1000, price falls to 500 → slave works for 500 (value). The outcome depends on which of the three factors is smallest.
The examples show that the slave's liability is capped by the least of the three measures.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وطولب بدينه لو حالا) يعني إذا كان الدين حالاً طالب المرتهن الراهن بعد العتق بالدين إذا كان موسراً لأنه إذا طولب بالرهن كان له أن يأخذه بدينه إذا كان من جنس حقه فيكون إيفاء واستيفاء فلا فائدة فيه. قال رحمه الله: (ولو مؤجلاً أخذ قيمة العبد وجعلت رهناً مكانه) يعني لو كان الدين مؤجلاً يؤخذ من المعتق قيمة العبد وتجعل رهناً مكان العبد إذا كان موسراً لأن قد تحقق، وفي التضمين فائدة وهي حصول الاستيثاق من الوجه الذي بيناه ويحبسها إلى حلول الأجل، فإذا حل اقتضاه بحقه إذا كان بجنسه لأن للغريم أن يستوفي حقه غريمه إذا ظفر بجنس حقه، وإن كان فيه فضل رده لانتهاء حكم الرهن بالاستيفاء، وإن كان حقه أقل من رجع بالزيادة لعدم ما يسقطه . قال رحمه الله : (ولو معسراً سعى العبد في الإقل من قيمته ومن الدين لأن حق المرتهن كان متعلقاً به فإذا تعذر الرجوع على المعتق لعسرته عليه لأنه رجع هو المنتفع بهذا العتق كما في عتق أحد الشريكين العبد المشترك، لأن الضمان بالجراح والغرم بالغنم وظاهر عبارة المؤلف أنه يسعى في الأقل من الشيئين المذكورين والمنقول في غيره أنه يسعى في الأقل من ثلاثة أشياء. قال في الجامع : أصله أن الراهن إذا أعتق المرهون وهو معسر ينظر إلى ثلاثة أشياء إلى قيمته يوم العتق، وإلى ما كان مضموناً بالدين، وإلى ما كان محبوساً به فإنه يسعى في الأقل من هذه الأشياء. أما القيمة فلأنه أحبس بالعتق من حق المرتهن هذا القدر فلا تلزمه السعاية إلا في هذا القدر كالعبد المشترك إذا أعتقه أحدهما وهو معسر، وأما المضمون بالدين إذا كان أقل لأن العبد مضمون بقدر الدين بالعتق وما يحدث بالزيادة المتصلة بعد القبض لم تصر مضمونة، وهذا لأن السعاية في حق الزيادة، فإن كانت محبوسة بالدين فلا يمكن ايجاب السعاية على العبد في حق الزيادة، وإن كان المحبوس أقل من المضمون ومن قيمته يسعى بقدره بأن رهن عبداً بألف قيمته ألف فأدى الراهن تسعمائة من الرهن ثم أعتقه وهو معسر يسعى العبد في مائة، فإن كان مضموناً بألف حتى لو هلك يهلك بألف لأنه محبوس بمائة فكان له أن يفتك بقدر مائة فكان العبد مضموناً بمائة من حيث اعتبار حالة الإعتاق رهن عبداً يساوي ألفاً بألف فصار يساوي خمسمائة بتراجع السعر ثم أعتقه الراهن وهو معسر يسعى العبد في خمسمائة لا غير، ولو كان المعتق الألف كلها لأن السعاية هنا أقل من الأشياء الثلاثة لأن السعاية خمسمائة والعبد موسراً ضمن مضمون بالدين، وذلك لأنه لو هلك يهلك بألف فإذا انتقص سعره وهو محبوس بألف فإن الراهن ما لم يؤد الألف لم يفتك الرهن ثم يقضي بالسعاية الدين وإن كان من جنس حقه وكان الدين حالاً فإن لم يكن من جنس حقه صرفه من جنس حقه كما تقدم، وإن كان الدين مؤجلاً جعلت السعاية رهناً، فإذا حل الأجل قضى به الدين على نحو ما ذكرنا.
He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: (And he is demanded for his debt if it is due) meaning if the debt is due, the mortgagee demands the pledgor after the freeing for the debt if he is solvent, because if he demands the pawn, he may take it for his debt if it is of the same type as his right, so it would be payment and collection, so there is no benefit in that. He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: (And if deferred, the value of the slave is taken and made a pawn in its place) meaning if the debt is deferred, the value of the slave is taken from the freeer and made a pawn in place of the slave if he is solvent, because it has been realized, and there is benefit in the guarantee, which is obtaining security in the manner we explained; and he detains it until the term arrives. When it arrives, he collects his right with it if it is of his type because the creditor may collect his right from his debtor if he finds his type of right; if there is a surplus, he returns it because the ruling of pawn ends with collection; if his right is less, he returns the excess because there is nothing to drop it. He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: (And if insolvent, the slave works for the lesser of his value and the debt) because the mortgagee's right was attached to him; when recourse to the freeer is prevented due to his insolvency, he (the slave) returns as the one benefiting from this freeing, as in the freeing of a jointly owned slave by one partner, because liability is according to injury, and gain is according to liability. The apparent expression of the author is that he works for the lesser of the two mentioned things. But it is transmitted from others that he works for the lesser of three things. He said in al-Jami': The principle is that when the pledgor frees the pawned slave while insolvent, we look at three things: his value on the day of freeing, what was guaranteed by the debt, and what he was detained for. He works for the lesser of these things. As for the value, because by the freeing he was detained from the mortgagee's right to this extent, so he is not liable for sa'yah except to this extent, like the jointly owned slave if one partner frees it while insolvent. As for the guaranteed amount if it is less: because the slave is guaranteed to the extent of the debt by the freeing, and what occurs by connected increase after possession is not guaranteed. This is because sa'yah is for the increase; if the detained amount is less than the guarantee and his value, he works to that extent. For example: he pawns a slave worth 1000 for a debt of 1000, the pledgor pays 900 of the debt from the pawn, then frees him while insolvent—the slave works for 100. If the guaranteed is 1000, i.e., if he perishes, he perishes for 1000, because he is detained for 1000, but the mortgagee can redeem for 1000 (actually 100? The example is garbled). Another example: he pawns a slave worth 1000 for 1000, so the price drops to 500, then he frees him while insolvent—the slave works for 500 only, not the whole 1000, because sa'yah here is less than the three things. Because the sa'yah is 500, and the slave is solvent? Actually the text says: 'and the slave is solvent but guaranteed by the debt'—this seems contradictory; probably meaning the slave is not insolvent, but the guarantee is for the debt. The passage continues: because if he perishes, he perishes for 1000, so when his price drops and he is detained for 1000, the pledgor cannot redeem without paying 1000. Then the slave pays the debt through sa'yah if it is of the same type and the debt is due; if not of the same type, he converts it; if deferred, the sa'yah becomes a pawn, and when the term comes, he pays the debt accordingly.
Source pages p. 484

Commentary
This passage presents three distinct rulings from the author of Kanz al-Daqaiq. First, if the debt is due and the pledgor is solvent after freeing, the mortgagee can demand the debt from the pledgor rather than taking the slave's value, because taking the pawn itself would be pointless if the debt is of the same type (it would just be an exchange). Second, if the debt is deferred and the pledgor is solvent, the value of the freed slave is taken and placed as a replacement pawn until the term ends; then the mortgagee collects from it. Third, if the pledgor is insolvent, the freed slave must work (sa'yah) to pay the lesser of his value or the debt. The commentator notes a difference: the author says 'lesser of two things' (value and debt), but in al-Jami' (a Hanafi source), it is the lesser of three: value, amount guaranteed by debt, and amount for which he is detained. The commentator explains the rationale using examples. The key principle is that the slave should not have to pay more than the actual loss to the mortgagee, and that the slave is considered the beneficiary of the freeing, so he must compensate. The discussion of the three things is detailed with cases of price fluctuations and partial payment of debt. This section is a ruling_statement without explicit proof (though reasons are given).

Key Terms
مُؤَجَّل (mu'ajjal): Debt with a deferred payment term.
سَعَى (sa‘ā): The slave works to earn money to pay an obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a pawned slave is freed by an insolvent pledgor, which of the following is NOT one of the three factors considered in al-Jami' for determining the slave's sa'yah?
A) The slave's value on the day of freeing
B) The amount guaranteed by the debt
C) The amount for which the slave was detained
D) The original purchase price of the slave

Key Takeaway
When a pawned slave is freed, the mortgagee's recourse depends on the debt's due status and the pledgor's solvency; if insolvent, the slave works for the least of value, guaranteed amount, or detained amount.

Two Differences Between Tadbeer and Freeing in Pawn
Setting out two differences between tadbeer and itq in pawn.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two differences between tadbeer and freeing (itq) in the context of a pawned slave, and apply the rule for sa'yah in each case.

Core Idea
In tadbeer, the slave works for the entire debt; in freeing, only for the lesser of three factors.

This passage from al-Asl specifies two scenarios where tadbeer (freeing upon death) differs from immediate freeing. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for correctly determining the slave's obligation to work (sa'yah) when the pledgor is solvent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the context
The passage compares tadbeer and itq for a pawned slave when the pledgor is solvent.
Both tadbeer and itq are forms of freeing, but tadbeer is effective only after the master's death.
2
Extract the first difference
In itq, the slave works for the lesser of three things (debt, value, earnings). In tadbeer, the slave works for the entire debt, regardless of amount.
The three factors: debt amount, slave's value, and earnings.
3
Extract the second difference
In tadbeer, the earnings go to the master; in itq, they go elsewhere (to the mortgagee).
This affects who benefits from the slave's labor.
4
Verify from al-Yanabi'
Al-Yanabi' adds that if the debt is due, the mudabbar works for the whole debt; if deferred, he works for his value which becomes a new pawn.
Shows the rule is consistent even with varying debt terms.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الأصل : إن كان مكان الإعتاق تدبير فالجواب فيه كالجواب في الإعتاق إلا في فصلين: أحدهما أن في فصل الإعتاق إن كان الراهن موسراً فالعبد يسعى في الأقل من أشياء، وفي التدبير يسعى في جميع الدين بالغاً ما بلغ. الثاني أن في التدبير بما سعى على المولى. وفي الينابيع : ولو دبره إن كان الدين حالاً سعى في الدين بالغاً ما بلغ، وإن كان مؤجلاً سعى في قيمته فتكون رهناً مكانه، وفي المحيط رهن جارية تساوي ألفاً بألفين فصارت إلى ألفين بزيادة السعر وولدت ولداً يساوي ألفاً يفتكها بألفين لأنها لو لم تزد لا يفتكها إلا بألفين فإن زادت أولى، وإذا هلكت هلكت بألفين لأن قيمتها . العقد ألف يوم والزيادة المتصلة لم يرد عليها عقد ولا قبض مقصود فكان وجودها وعدمها بمنزلة. وإن أعتقها المولى وهو معسر سعت في الألف، وكذلك لو أعتقها سعياً في الألف ورجعا بذلك على المولى ورجع المرتهن ببقية دينه لأن الراهن لما أعتقهما صار بإعتاق الولد قابضاً للولد حكماً كالمشتري إذا أعتق المبيع قبل القبض فيقسم الدين عليهما فيسعيان في الألف لأنها أقل ورجعا بذلك على المولى لأنهما أديا دينه من خالص ملكهما لأنهما من قيمتهما يوم العتق يسعيان وهما حران، ومن أدى ثلاثة وأدى دين الغير من خالص ملكه وهو مجبر عليه فعليه الرجوع على من عليه الدين إذا لم يسلم له العوض ولم يسلم للعبد ما كان للمرتهن من حق الحبس في
And in al-Asl: If the disposition was tadbeer instead of freeing, the answer is the same as for freeing except in two aspects: one, that in the case of freeing if the pledgor is solvent, the slave works for the lesser of the things, while in tadbeer he works for the entire debt however much it is. Second, that in tadbeer, what he earns goes to the master. And in al-Yanabi': If he makes him mudabbar, if the debt is due, he works for the debt however much it is; if deferred, he works for his value, which becomes a pawn in his place. And in al-Muhit: He pawns a female slave worth 1000 for 2000, then her price rises to 2000, and she gives birth to a child worth 1000. He redeems her for 2000 because if she had not increased, he would not redeem except for 2000; so if she increments, it is more appropriate. And if she perishes, she perishes for 2000 because her ... the contract (value) on the day (of pawn) was 1000, and the connected increase was not subject to contract nor intended possession, so its existence and non-existence are the same. And if the master frees her while insolvent, she works for the 1000 (value?). Similarly, if he frees both (mother and child), they work for 1000, and they recoup from the master, and the mortgagee recovers the rest of his debt because when the pledgor freed both, by freeing the child he became a deemed possessor of the child like a buyer who frees the purchased item before possession. So the debt is divided between them, and they both work for the 1000 because it is less, and they recoup from the master because they paid the debt of another from their pure property, as they work based on their value on the day of freeing while they are free. And one who pays three things and pays the debt of another from his pure property while compelled, must recoup from the one on whom the debt was due if no consideration is given to him, and the slave does not get what the mortgagee had of the right of detention in... [text cuts off]
Source pages p. 485

Commentary
This passage presents additional rulings from other Hanafi sources (al-Asl, al-Yanabi', al-Muhit). It highlights two differences between tadbeer and freeing (itq): (1) When the pledgor is solvent, in freeing the slave works for the lesser of the three factors, but in tadbeer the slave works for the entire debt (because the master keeps earnings). (2) In tadbeer, the earnings go to the master. Then it discusses a case from al-Yanabi' where if the debt is due, the mudabbar works for the whole debt; if deferred, he works for his value which becomes a new pawn. Then a detailed case from al-Muhit: a female slave worth 1000 is pawned for 2000, her price rises to 2000, and she gives birth to a child worth 1000. The owner redeems her for 2000 despite the increase (since the original debt is 2000). If she perishes, she is lost for 2000 because the rise in value is not considered part of the pawn contract. If the owner frees her while insolvent, she works for 1000 (her original value). If he frees both mother and child, they split the debt (1000) and work for it, then recoup from the master. This passage is complex and deals with multiple scenarios. The text cuts off mid-sentence at the end of the window.

Key Terms
تدبير (tadbeer): A form of freeing a slave effective after the master's death; the slave is a mudabbar.
إعتاق (itq): Immediate freeing of a slave.
سعاية (sa'yah): The slave's work to earn money to pay off the debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the key difference between tadbeer and freeing when the pledgor is solvent?
A) In freeing, the slave works for the entire debt; in tadbeer, for lesser.
B) In tadbeer, the slave works for the entire debt; in freeing, for lesser.
C) Both are the same.
D) In tadbeer, the slave does not work at all.

Key Takeaway
In tadbeer, the slave must work for the full debt regardless of his value or earnings, unlike freeing where he works for the lesser of three factors.

Rulings on a Pawned Female Slave Giving Birth
Detailed case analysis of a pawned female slave giving birth, with rulings on redemption, loss, and manumission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the increase in value and birth of a child affect the redemption and loss of a pawned female slave, and apply the rules for sa'yah when she is freed.

Core Idea
A pawned female slave's increase in value and child are not part of the pawn; she is redeemed at the original debt amount, and the child is treated separately.

This passage from al-Muhit presents a complex case: a female slave worth 1000 is pawned for 2000, her price rises, and she gives birth. It then covers scenarios of her death and manumission. Understanding these rulings clarifies how connected increases and offspring are treated in pawn contracts.

Guided Path
1
Understand the initial scenario
A female slave worth 1000 is pawned for 2000. Her value then rises to 2000, and she gives birth to a child worth 1000.
The debt is 2000, original value 1000, rise to 2000.
2
Analyze redemption
The master redeems her for 2000 (original debt), not for the increased value. The child is not part of the pawn.
Because the increase is connected and not contracted upon, it does not affect the redemption amount.
3
Analyze loss (perishing)
If she dies, she perishes for 2000 (the debt amount), not her value at death. The increase is ignored.
The connected increase is considered non-existent for pawn purposes.
4
Analyze manumission (itq) when insolvent
If the master frees her while insolvent, she works for her original value (1000), not the increased value or debt.
Same if he frees both mother and child—they split the debt (1000) and work, then recoup from master.

Key Terms
جَارِيَة (jāriyah): A female slave; in this context, one who gives birth while pawned.
زيادة متصلة (ziyada muttasila): An increase that is physically connected to the pawned item, such as weight gain or price rise.
قبض حكمي (qabd hukmi): Deemed possession; possession by operation of law rather than physical taking.

Tadbir of Mortgaged Slaves: When Does Tadbir Constitute Legal Receipt?
Explains tadbir and sa'ayah for offsetting debt in mortgage scenarios.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that tadbir is considered qabd only when it does not harm the mortgagee, and derive the correct sa'ayah obligation in multi-generational scenarios.

Core Idea
Tadbir is not qabd in reality, but is considered qabd only when harmless to the mortgagee.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq tackles a nuanced problem: where a mortgaged slave is declared mudabbara, does this count as the master taking legal receipt (qabd) of the slave? The answer affects how debt is divided among offspring. The Hanafi school applies a harm-based criterion: tadbir is treated as qabd only if it does not harm the mortgagee's right to sa'ayah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its effect
The act is tadbir of a mortgaged slave. The effect in question is whether tadbir makes the master a constructive receiver (qabd hukmi) of the slave, thereby dividing the debt among the slave and her offspring.
Tadbir is a conditional emancipation, not a transfer of possession.
2
State the Hanafi position on tadbir as qabd
Abu Hanifa and the majority hold that tadbir is not actual qabd but is considered legal qabd only when it benefits or does not harm the mortgagee. Otherwise, it is not considered qabd.
The principle: 'Tadbir is like emancipation in being a constructive destruction; it is considered qabd only when no harm.'
3
Identify the opposing view: 'Isa b. Abban
'Isa b. Abban argued that tadbir always constitutes qabd, because it transfers constructive possession. Thus, after tadbir of multiple slaves, the debt divides equally among them. In the given case, after two die, the remaining one owes two-thirds.
His analogy: if all were mortgaged and then taken into possession (qabd haqiqi), the same division would occur.
4
Evaluate the harm in the current case
If tadbir were considered qabd, the mortgagee's right to sa'ayah would drop from half the debt to a tiny fraction (1/11). This is harmful, so tadbir is not considered qabd here. The offspring serves for half the debt.
The key distinction: in some cases tadbir as qabd benefits the mortgagee; there it is applied.
5
Formulate the mufta bihi ruling
The relied-upon position is that the lower offspring serves for half the debt (500) when the mother and grandmother die after tadbir. 'Isa's view (two-thirds) is rejected because tadbir is not qabd when harmful.
This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and affirmed by later authorities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الرهن باب التصرف في الرهن والجناية عليه وجنايته على غيره لأنه إحداهما سعت الباقية في نصف الدين ويضمن المولى نصفه لأنها ماتت بعدما خرجت من الرهن بالتدبير ولا يتحول شيء من دين الميتة إلى الباقية لأن الباقية لم تكن متولدة من الميتة والميتة في السعاية كانت محتملة على المولى، فإذا ماتت قبل استيفاء السعاية فقد تعذر استيفاء حقه من جهة المحتمل وهو الكفيل فيطالب من الأصيل، فإن ولدت هذه الباقية ثم ماتت يسعى الولد فيما على أمه وسواء كانت قيمة الأم أقل أو أكثر لأنها ولدت بمثل حالها مدبرة فيسري ما فيها إلى ولدها ولو كانت قبل التدبير ثم دبرهما جميعاً سعت في مائتين وخمسين إن كانت قيمتها مثل قيمة الأم لأن الولد قبل التدبير صار رهناً فانقسم ما في الأم من الدين عليهما نصفين على سبيل التوفيق إن ورد على الولد قبض الرهن بقي كذلك منقسماً، وإن لم يرد عليه قبض بطل الانقسام وظهر أن الدين كله كان بإزاء الأم، وهنا ورد على الراهن قبض على الولد لما ذكرنا لأن التدبير من المشتري قبل القبض يصير به قابضاً. رهن أمة بألف وقيمتها ألف فولدت ولداً يساوي ألفاً فماتت الأم ثم دبر البنت عليها السعاية في خمسمائة ورد على الميت قبض الراهن فإنه بالتدبير صار قابضاً للولد فظهر أن الدين كان منقسماً عليهما نصفين، فإن ولدت البنت بنتاً وماتت البنت الأولى سعت السفلى في خمسمائة وإن كانت قيمتها مائة لأن السفلى ولد المستسعاة فسرى ما في أمها إليها. ولدت الأمة المرهونة بنتاً ثم ولدت البنت بنتاً وقيمة كل واحدة ألف ثم دبرهن جميعاً ثم ماتت الأم والبنت الأولى فعلى السفلى السعاية في نصف الدين وعن عيسى بن أبان قال : ينبغي أن تسعى في ثلثي الدين لأنه قد كان قابضاً للوسطى بالتدبير لأن التدبير قبض وصار بإزاء كل واحدة منهن الدين كما لو رهنهن جميعاً ثم دبرهن وهو معسر وقد ماتت بنتان قبل السعاية تسعى الباقية في ثلثي الدين فكذا هذا والجواب عنه أن التدبير ليس بقبض حقيقة ولكن اعتبر قبضاً حكماً بحكم الإتلاف كالإعتاق وإنما يعتبر قبضاً حكماً متى لم يكن في اعتباره قبضاً ضرر على المرتهن، وهنا في اعتباره قبضاً ضرر بالمرتهن لأنه يؤدي إلى إبطال حقه بالسعاية لأنه لم يعتبر قبضاً كان للمرتهن أن يستسعي السفلى في نصف الدين، ومتى اعتبر قبضاً يستسعيها في جزء واحد من أحد عشر جزءاً من الدين فلا يعتبر قابضاً دفعاً للضرر عنه فصار كأن الوسطى ماتت قبل التدبير فيصير بإزاء السفلى نصف الدين بخلاف المسألة المتقدمة لأنا لو اعتبرنا التدبير قبضاً ينتفع به المرتهن ولا يتضرر به لأن السفلى تسعى في جميع ما وجب على الوسطى، ومتى لم يعتبر قبضاً تسعى في جزء من أحد عشر حزءاً من الدين، وكذلك لو دبر السفلى بعدما ماتت الأم والجدة لأنه لا يحتسب بالوسطى إذا ماتت قبل التدبير فكأنها لم تكن ولدت الجدة إلا ولداً واحداً ثم دبر الولد ولدت أمة الرهن ولداً يساوي ألفا ثم دبرها فعلى كل واحد منهما سعاية في خمسمائة لما عرف وإن ماتت البنت سعت الأم في الألف كلها. طعن عيسى وقال : بالتدبير يقرر الضمان فيه ولا يعود إلى الأم. ثلث متی [؟] قيمته ومن الدين ويرجع به على سيده واتلاف الرهن كإعتاقه وإن أتلفه أجنبي فالمرتهن والجواب أن التدبير متى اعتبر قبضاً لا يتضرر به المرتهن بل ينتفع به لأنه متى اعتبر قبضاً تهلك الأم بخمسمائة ويسعى في خمسمائة، ومتى لم يعتبر قبضاً تهلك الأم بجميع فيعتبر قبضاً فيكون مقبوضاً بالتدبير فصار كأنه رهنهما ثم دبرهما رهن أمة تساوي ألفاً بألف إلى أجل فولدت ولداً يساوي ألفاً فدبر المولى الولد وهو موسر ضمن قيمته ويكون رهناً مع الأم، فإن كان معسراً يسعى الولد في خمسمائة لأن المولى جان في التدبير أتلف حق المرتهن وحق المرتهن في الحبس كان ثابتاً في الكل فضمن قيمته وأما المدبر غير جان فيسعى بقدر حق المرتهن في الولد وهو خمسمائة لا بقدر قيمته لتظهر مزية غير الجاني على الجاني، فإن مات قبل السعاية كانت الأم رهناً بالألف، وإن هلكت الأم تهلك بنصف الدين، وعند عيسى تسعى في خمسمائة والصحيح جواب الكتاب لأن الولد صار محبوساً في الرهن لأنه بالتدبير صار مقبوضاً لأنه لا ضرر في صيرورته مقبوضاً محبوساً بالرهن على المرتهن بل فيه منفعة فإنه لا يسقط بهلاك أحدهما إلا نصف الدين فصار كأنه رهنهما ثم أخذهما وهو معسر ثم ماتت إحداهما صارت الباقية رهناً بالألف، ولو ماتت الباقية تموت بخمسمائة فكذا هذا. وفي الفتاوى الغياثية : ولو استولدها أو دبرها لا يحبس بالدين ويضمن إن كان موسراً وبيعت في الدين إن كان معسراً ولا يستسعي الولد إن كانت الدعوى قبل الانفصال. فإن قال قضاء هو من دينك جاز، وإن كانت قبل الحلول سعى في قيمته. ولو رهنا عبداً فأعتقه أحد الراهنين وهو موسر ضمن نصف قيمته لشريكه ونصفه للمرتهن ويؤدي الشريك ذلك إلى المرتهن، وإن العبد في الدين ورجع بنصفه على المعتق، وكذا المعسر الراهن إذا أعتقه ضمن قيمته ورجع على الراهن أو على المعتق ثم رجع هو على الراهن. ولو انتقص سعره فأعتقه الراهن ضمن قيمته أعتق، ولو كان زادت قيمته ضمن قيمته يوم الرهن، وإن كان معسراً فالسعاية كذلك، وكذا لو ولدت الأمة فأعتقها الراهن سعى في قيمة الأم يوم الرهن، وإن كان الدين أكثر في التدبير يسعى في الدين قال رحمه الله : (ويرجع به على سيده) يعني العبد بالسعاية على سيده إذا Because one of them, the remaining one served for half the debt, and the master guarantees half of it because she died after leaving the mortgage by tadbir, and nothing of the debt of the deceased transfers to the remaining one because the remaining one was not born from the deceased, and the deceased in sa'ayah was a guarantor for the master. So if she died before the sa'ayah was fulfilled, then his right from the guarantor (the surety) became impossible to obtain, so he demands from the principal. If this remaining one gives birth and then dies, the child serves for what was upon his mother, whether the mother's value is less or more, because she gave birth while in the same condition, being mudabbara, so what was upon her extends to her child. And if it was before tadbir, then he declares tadbir on both together, she serves for two hundred and fifty if her value is like the mother's value, because the child before tadbir became a mortgage, so what was in the mother from the debt divided between them in two halves on the basis of al-tawfiq. A slave-girl mortgaged for a thousand, her value a thousand, then she gave birth to a child worth a thousand, then the mother died, then he declared tadbir on the daughter: upon her is sa'ayah for five hundred, and receipt of the mortgagor is returned upon the deceased, because by tadbir he became a receiver of the child, so it appears that the debt was divided between them in half. So upon the lower one is sa'ayah for half the debt. And from 'Isa b. Abban he said: It is appropriate that she serve for two-thirds of the debt, because he had become a receiver of the middle one by tadbir, because tadbir is qabd, and the debt became against each one of them just as if he mortgaged all of them, then declared tadbir on them while he is insolvent, and two daughters died before sa'ayah, so the remaining one serves for two-thirds of the debt. So this is similar. The answer to it is that tadbir is not qabd in reality, but is considered qabd legally by virtue of destruction like emancipation. It is only considered qabd legally when there is no harm to the mortgagee in considering it qabd. And here, considering it qabd harms the mortgagee because it leads to nullifying his right to sa'ayah. Because if it is not considered qabd, the mortgagee has the right to make the lower one serve for half the debt; but if it is considered qabd, he makes her serve for one part out of eleven parts of the debt. So it is not considered qabd to repel harm from him. So it becomes as if the middle one died before tadbir, so against the lower one is half the debt, unlike the previous case because if we considered tadbir as qabd, the mortgagee would benefit and not be harmed, because the lower one serves for all that was due upon the middle one; and if it is not considered qabd, she serves for one part out of eleven parts of the debt. Similarly, if he declared tadbir on the lower one after the mother and grandmother died, because the middle one is not counted if she died before tadbir, so it is as if the grandmother gave birth to only one child, then he declared tadbir on the child. The slave-girl of the mortgage gave birth to a child worth a thousand, then he declared tadbir on her, so upon each one of them is sa'ayah for five hundred as known, and if the daughter dies, the mother serves for the entire thousand. 'Isa objected and said: By tadbir the guarantee is established in it and does not return to the mother. [؟] his value and from the debt and he returns to his master; and destruction of the mortgage is like its emancipation; and if a third party destroys it, the mortgagee... The answer is that when tadbir is considered qabd, the mortgagee is not harmed but benefits, because if considered qabd, the mother perishes with five hundred and he serves for five hundred; and if not considered qabd, the mother perishes with all. So it is considered qabd, and so it becomes as if he mortgaged both of them, then declared tadbir on them. A slave-girl worth a thousand mortgaged for a thousand with a term, then she gave birth to a child worth a thousand, then the master declared tadbir on the child while he is wealthy: he guarantees its value and it becomes a mortgage with the mother. If he is insolvent, the child serves for five hundred, because the master is a wrongdoer in tadbir, having destroyed the right of the mortgagee; and the right of the mortgagee in detention was established in the whole, so he guarantees its value. As for the mudabbir who is not a wrongdoer, he serves according to the right of the mortgagee in the child, which is five hundred, not its value, to show the superiority of the non-wrongdoer over the wrongdoer. If he dies before sa'ayah, the mother remains mortgaged for the thousand; if the mother perishes, she perishes with half the debt. According to 'Isa, she serves for five hundred; and the correct answer is the answer of the book because the child became detained in the mortgage because by tadbir it became a receiver (maqbud), because there is no harm in its becoming a receiver detained in the mortgage for the mortgagee; rather, there is benefit, because with the destruction of either one, only half the debt is lost. So it becomes as if he mortgaged both of them, then took them while insolvent, then one of them died: the remaining one becomes mortgaged for the thousand; and if the remaining one dies, it dies with five hundred. So this is similar. And in al-Fatawa al-Ghiyathiyya: If he makes her an umm walad or declares tadbir on her, she is not detained for the debt; he guarantees if wealthy, and she is sold for the debt if insolvent; and the child does not perform sa'ayah if the claim was before separation. If he says 'Payment is from your debt', it is permissible; and if it was before the term, he serves for its value. And if two people mortgage a slave and one of the mortgagors emancipates him while wealthy, he guarantees half his value to his partner and half to the mortgagee; and the partner pays that to the mortgagee; and the slave is in the debt and he returns with half to the emancipator. Similarly, if the insolvent mortgagor emancipates him, he guarantees his value and he returns to the mortgagor or to the emancipator, then he returns to the mortgagor. And if his price decreased and the mortgagor emancipates him, he guarantees his value on the day of emancipation; and if it increased, he guarantees his value on the day of mortgage; and if he is insolvent, then sa'ayah is similar. Similarly, if the slave-girl gives birth and the mortgagor emancipates her, he serves for the value of the mother on the day of mortgage; and if the debt is more, in tadbir he serves for the debt. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And he returns to his master) meaning the slave by sa'ayah to his master when he becomes wealthy, because he paid his debt while he was compelled, and he was not a volunteer, so he becomes like the lender of the mortgage. Unlike the slave performing sa'ayah if he is between two partners and one of them emancipates his share while insolvent, and he serves for the share of the other and pays, because it is not obligatory upon him because he serves to complete emancipation according to them and to obtain emancipation according to Imam; and here he serves in guarantee for insolvency after complete emancipation, so they differ. So Imam made sa'ayah obligatory on the jointly-owned slave in both cases of wealth and insolvency, and on the mortgaged slave only in case of insolvency, because what is established for the mortgagee is a right of ownership, and what is established for the partner is true ownership, and the right of ownership is lower than true ownership, so sa'ayah was obligatory on it only in case of necessity; and on the higher in both cases to show the difference between them. Source pages p. 487

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses complex rulings regarding tadbir (declaration that a slave is free upon the master's death) of mortgaged slaves and the subsequent sa'ayah (earning to pay off debt) obligations. It begins with a scenario where one of two mortgaged slave-girls serves for half the debt, then dies after being mudabbara, and the master guarantees half. The key principle is that the offspring of a mudabbara inherit her liability because the child is born in the same condition (mudabbara). The passage then examines multiple cases: tadbir before birth vs after, the effect of qabd (receipt) on division of debt, and a detailed dispute with 'Isa b. Abban regarding whether tadbir constitutes legal qabd. The Hanafi position, as articulated in the book, is that tadbir is not actual qabd but is considered qabd legally only when it does not harm the mortgagee. In cases where considering it qabd would reduce the mortgagee's right to sa'ayah (e.g., from half to a tiny fraction), it is not considered qabd. The correct view is that the lower offspring serves for half the debt, not two-thirds as 'Isa claimed. The passage then covers: a mortgage with a term, distinction between wealthy and insolvent masters, a fatwa from Fatawa al-Ghiyathiyya regarding umm walad and tadbir, and the case of two co-mortgagors one of whom frees the slave. Throughout, the Hanafi school emphasizes the primacy of the mortgagee's right of detention (haqq al-habs) and the need to avoid harming it. The commentary follows the author's order, explaining each scenario and the underlying reasoning based on istihsan (juristic preference) and qiyas.

Key Terms
تدبير (tadbir): A declaration by a master that his slave will be free upon the master's death.
سعاية (sa'ayah): Effort or work performed by a slave to earn money to pay off a debt or obligation.
قبض (qabd): Physical or legal receipt/taking possession of an object of sale or mortgage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position in this passage, if a mortgaged slave-girl (value 1000) and her daughter (value 1000) both become mudabbara, and the mother dies, and the daughter dies, what portion of the debt (total 1000) does the granddaughter serve?
A) Half the debt (500)
B) Two-thirds of the debt (666.67)
C) The entire debt (1000)
D) One-third of the debt (333.33)

Key Takeaway
Tadbir of a mortgaged slave is considered legal receipt (qabd) only when it does not harm the mortgagee's right to sa'ayah; otherwise, the original debt division stands.

Returning the Pledge as a Loan: Possession and Liability
This passage is a ruling with talil about returning the pledge as a loan to the pledgor.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the effect of returning the pledge as a loan to the pledgor on the mortgagee's liability and explain the rationale based on possession.

Core Idea
Possession is the basis of liability; returning the pledge removes possession and therefore liability.

In this lesson, we examine the first scenario from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: when a mortgagee voluntarily returns the pledged item to the pledgor as a loan. The text explains that this act removes the mortgagee's liability because liability is tied to possession (qabd). We will unpack the ruling and its talil, and see how the principle applies when the pledge perishes in the pledgor's hand.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? The mortgagee lends the pledged item to the pledgor. The ruling: the mortgagee's liability (daman) drops.
This is the main ruling of the passage.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is talil (reasoning): liability was based on possession, and possession was nullified by returning the item to its owner.
The text explicitly states 'because liability was based on his possession and it was invalidated by returning to its owner'.
3
Trace the legal link
Possession (qabd) is the cause of liability. By returning the item to the pledgor, the mortgagee loses possession, and thus the liability ends.
This is a core Hanafi principle: daman follows possession.
4
Note the consequence
If the pledge perishes in the pledgor's hand after the loan, it perishes without compensation (majjanan). The mortgagee bears no loss.
This confirms that liability is fully removed.

And it came out from his lending it to its pledgor: meaning if the mortgagee lends the pledge to the pledgor, it leaves the liability of the mortgagee because the liability was based on his possession and it was invalidated by returning to its owner, so liability is removed. He said: And each has the right to return it as a pledge meaning each of the pledgor and mortgagee has a right in the pledge, so he may return it as a pledge in its place due to the continuation of the contract of pledge as we explained, unlike if one of them rents it or sells it or gives it as a gift to the mortgagee or a stranger before he re-pledges it, then it does not return as a pledge except with a new contract. And if the pledgor dies, the mortgagee is like other creditors because these transactions invalidate the pledge, unlike the loan and deposit because they are not binding. And if the pledgor permits the mortgagee to use or lend for work, then the pledge perishes before he begins work, it perishes against the debt due to the basis of the pledge contract; similarly if it perishes after finishing work due to the removal of the trust hand; and if it perishes during work, it perishes as a trust. And if they differ regarding the time of perishing, and the mortgagee claims that it perished during work and the pledgor claims that it perished before finishing work, the word is that of the mortgagee because he denies, and the evidence is that of the pledgor because he claims.
Source pages p. 490

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the rulings of pledge (rahn) when the mortgagee returns the pledge to the pledgor as a loan (‘ariyah). The key principle is that the mortgagee’s liability (daman) is based on possession (qabd). When the mortgagee voluntarily returns the pledge to the pledgor, possession is lost, and so the mortgagee is no longer liable if the pledge perishes in the pledgor’s hand. The text also covers scenarios: if the pledgor then returns it to the mortgagee, liability revives. If the pledgor dies before reclaiming, the mortgagee remains a secured creditor. The passage then addresses lending the pledge to a third party with both parties’ consent—liability drops. Each party may return the pledge to its status as a pledged item. The author distinguishes this from sale or gift, which terminate the pledge contract. Finally, the passage discusses destruction during authorized use: if the mortgagee uses the pledge with permission, perishing before use is against the debt, after use is a trust, and during use is also a trust (amanah). Disputes about timing are resolved with the mortgagee's word and the pledgor's evidence.

Key Terms
عارية (‘āriyah): A loan of a chattel for use without compensation.
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability for the value of the pledge if it is destroyed while in the mortgagee's possession.
قبض (qabḍ): Physical possession that triggers liability and security rights.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a mortgagee returns the pledged item to the pledgor as a loan (ariyah) and the item is then destroyed in the pledgor's hand, who bears the loss?
A) The mortgagee, because the pledge contract is still in effect.
B) The pledgor, because the mortgagee's liability was based on possession and that possession has been lost.
C) Both share the loss equally.
D) The mortgagee, because the return was voluntary.

Key Takeaway
Returning the pledge to the pledgor as a loan removes the mortgagee's liability because liability is based on possession, not the contract.

Borrowing a Garment to Pledge It: Validity, Specification, and Liability
A detailed ruling on borrowing for pledge with sub-issues

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on borrowing a garment to pledge it, identify when the borrower becomes liable for violating the lender's specifications, and apply the rules to factual scenarios.

Core Idea
Borrowing to pledge is valid, but violating the lender's specification (tasmiyah) makes the borrower liable.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra’iq addresses a practical scenario: someone borrows a garment with the express purpose of pledging it to secure a debt. The author first establishes the validity of such a borrowing, relying on the Hanafi distinction between ownership of the substance (milk al-‘ayn) and ownership of the hand (milk al-yad). He then explains the consequences when the lender specifies the amount, person, or place of the pledge and the borrower deviates from those specifications. Finally, he provides rules for resolving disputes about loss or retrieval. Understanding these rules is crucial for anyone engaged in lending or borrowing for security purposes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The act is borrowing (isti‘ārah) a garment for the purpose of pledging it. The default ruling is that it is valid (sahih) because the lender voluntarily grants a limited right of possession (milk al-yad) to the borrower, which can exist separately from the full ownership (milk al-‘ayn).
This is based on the principle that milk al-yad can be transferred without transferring milk al-‘ayn, as seen in sale where ownership passes but possession may remain.
2
Distinguish absolute permission from specification
If the lender gives absolute permission (without specifying amount, person, or place), the borrower may pledge the garment for any amount and type, analogous to borrowing an animal without specifying its use. However, if the lender specifies any of these, the borrower must adhere—otherwise liability (ḍamān) arises.
The text emphasizes that specification (tasmiyah) creates binding conditions because the lender's consent is limited.
3
Analyze the scenarios of specification violation
When the lender specifies an amount, pledging for less harms the lender (part becomes trust) and pledging for more makes redemption difficult. When the value is less than the specified amount, pledging for the actual value avoids liability, but pledging for a different species (e.g., food instead of dirhams) incurs liability. Similarly, pledging to a different person or in a different place violates the lender's trust and causes harm.
In each case, the borrower becomes liable because he causes extra harm (ḍarar) beyond what the lender consented to.
4
Understand the rules of dispute and recovery
If the borrower and lender disagree about loss or deficiency, the borrower's word is taken (with oath) and the lender must provide evidence. If the pledgor and mortgagee agree that the borrower retrieved the pledge before redemption, the pledgor is believed, and the lender can recover from the pledgor the amount of debt discharged.
This follows the general principle that the claimant (lender) must prove his claim, and the defendant (borrower) swears to his statement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

يجعل كله مضموناً، وأما إذا رهنه بأكثر فلأنه قد يحتاج المعير إلى الفكاك ليصير إلى ملكه وربما يتعسر عليه الفكاك متى زادت على المسمى لأنه قد لا يجد الزيادة على المسمى فيتضرر به وهو قد رضي بضمان قليل ولم يرض بقضاء دين كثير فصار مخالفاً. وإن كانت قيمة الثوب أقل من المسمى بأن أعار ثوباً ليرهنه بعشرة وقيمته تسعة فإن رهن بقدر قيمته تسعة لا يضمن، وأما إذا رهنه بجنس آخر ضمن في الفصول كلها لأن مقصوده من تسمية الدراهم أن يرجع عليه بالدراهم متى هلك الثوب، ومتى رهن بالطعام لا يمكنه الرجوع عليه بالدراهم، ولأنه ربما يحتاج إلى انفكاك وربما يتيسر له الكفاك بالدراهم ويتعسر عليك الفكاك بالطعام فيلحقه يزادة ضرر. وأما إذا أعاره ليرهنه من إنسان بعينه وفرهنه من غيره ضمن لأنه ربما يحتاج إلى أن يقضي دينه لاستخلاص ملكه والناس يتفاوتون في القضاء والاقتضاء فكذلك في الحفظ والأمانة فالرضا بحفظ زيد لا يكون رضا بحفظ عمرو فالخلاف يخلفه زيادة ضرر. ولو أعاره ليرهنه بالكوفة فرهنه بالبصرة ضمن لأن البلدان والأمكنة متفاوتة في الحفظ والصيانة ولأنه يخاف خطر الطريق متى نقل، ولأنه قد يتيسر له الفكاك في المكان المشروط ويتعسر عليه الفكاك في غيره، وإذا اختلفا في الهلاك أو النقصان قبل الاسترداد من المرتهن أو بعده فالقول للمستعير والبينة للمعير لأنه يدعي قضاء دينه من ينكر، فإن ادعى الراهن أن المستعير استرد الرهن قبل الافتكاك وصدقه المرتهن يصدق الراهن لأن الراهن والمرتهن تصادقا على فسخ الرهن والرهن عقد جرى بينهما فيكون ماله والقول وقولهما أنهما فسخا ذلك كما في المتبايعين لأن المعير ادعى أنه قضى دينه من وأنكر الراهن فيكون القول قوله ويرجع المعير على الراهن بقدر ما يذهب عنه بالدين لأنه قد صار قاضياً دينه من ماله بهذا القدر بأمره، فإذا هلك عند المستعير قبل الرهن أو بعد ماله والمستعير
He said (may Allah have mercy on him): And if he borrows a garment to pledge it, it is valid because he is voluntarily establishing ownership of the hand, so it is considered voluntary establishment of ownership of the substance and the hand, and it is permissible for ownership of the hand to separate from ownership of the substance in establishment for the mortgagee just as it separates for the sake of sale in removal because sale removes ownership without the hand, so it becomes a pledge for whatever he pledged it for, little or much, when he gives him absolute discretion. He said in al-Mabsut: His issues are on chapters: one of them on the modality of the borrowing, the second on their difference regarding perishing and deficiency, and the third on liability for both. Chapter: Then if he borrows a garment to pledge it, it is either that he did not specify anything for him, or he specified something for him, or he specified a person or a place. If he borrows a garment to pledge it and specifies a place or a person for it, he may pledge it for any amount and any type he wishes because he asked him to repay his debt from this wealth absolutely because the pledge is pledged for repayment and receipt by legal construction, and if he asked him to repay his debt from his wealth, it is permissible, and similarly this. If the borrowing is found to be absolute, then the lender has consented to pledge it for whatever he wishes, just as if he borrowed from a man an animal without specifying what to do with it, he may ride, make someone else ride, and load it, and similarly this. And if he specifies a determined amount and he pledges for less or more: if their values are equal or more, and he pledges for less than what was specified, then the lender is harmed because part of it becomes a trust with the mortgagee, and he did not consent to that; rather he asked that all of it be guaranteed. As for if he pledges for more, because the lender may need to redeem to get it back into his ownership, and perhaps redemption may become difficult if it exceeds the specified amount because he may not find the excess over the specified, so he is harmed, and he had consented to a small guarantee and did not consent to paying a large debt, so he became violative. And if the value of the garment is less than the specified amount, for example he borrows a garment to pledge it for ten and its value is nine, if he pledges it for its value of nine, he is not liable. As for if he pledges it for a different species, he is liable in all chapters because his purpose in specifying dirhams is that he would recourse against him for dirhams if the garment perishes, and if he pledges for food, he cannot recourse against him for dirhams; and because he may need redemption and perhaps redemption with dirhams is easy for him but redemption with food is difficult, so extra harm befalls him. As for if he borrows it to pledge it to a specific person but he pledges it to someone else, he is liable because he may need to pay his debt to release his property, and people differ in giving and taking, similarly in guarding and trust; consent to Zayd's guarding is not consent to 'Amr's guarding, so differing causes extra harm. And if he borrows it to pledge it in Kufa but he pledges it in Basra, he is liable because cities and places differ in guarding and maintenance, and because he fears the danger of the road if transported, and because redemption may be easy in the specified place but difficult elsewhere. And if they differ regarding the perishing or deficiency before retrieval from the mortgagee or after, the word is that of the borrower and the evidence is that of the lender because he claims repayment of his debt and the other denies. If the pledgor claims that the borrower retrieved the pledge before redemption and the mortgagee confirms him, the pledgor is believed because the pledgor and mortgagee have mutually agreed on the dissolution of the pledge, and the pledge is a contract between them, so it is their affair, and their word is that they dissolved it just as in the case of two sellers, because the lender claims that he repaid his debt from his property and the pledgor denies, so the word is his, and the lender recourses against the pledgor to the extent of what goes from him due to the debt because he became one who repaid his debt from his property to this extent by his order. So if it perishes with the borrower before the pledge or after his property and the borrower
Source pages p. 491

Commentary
This passage addresses the borrowing of a garment specifically for the purpose of pledging it. The author first establishes that such a borrowing is valid: the lender grants the borrower the right to use the garment as a pledge, which is a limited form of ownership of the hand (milk al-yad) separate from ownership of the substance (milk al-ayn). The borrower can then pledge it for any amount if the lender gives absolute discretion. The passage then details the effects of specification. If the lender specifies a person, place, or amount, the borrower must adhere; otherwise, he becomes liable (daman) for the garment because he causes harm to the lender. For example, if the lender specifies a certain amount and the borrower pledges for less, the lender is harmed because part of the garment becomes unsecured. If the borrower pledges for more, the lender may face difficulty in redeeming. If the value of the garment is less than the specified loan amount, and the borrower pledges for the actual value, he is not liable. However, if he pledges for a different species (e.g., food instead of dirhams), he is liable because the lender cannot recover the same species. Similar rules apply for specifying a person or place. The passage concludes with rules for disputes: if the borrower and lender disagree about destruction, the borrower's word is taken with the lender's evidence. If the pledgor and mortgagee agree that the borrower retrieved the pledge, the pledgor is believed, and the lender can recourse against the pledgor for the amount of debt discharged.

Key Terms
استعار (ista‘āra): To borrow a chattel for use without compensation.
ملك اليد (milk al-yad): Ownership of the hand, meaning the right to possess and use the item temporarily, as opposed to ownership of the substance (milk al-‘ayn).
تسمية (tasmiyah): Specification of the amount, person, or place for which the garment is to be pledged.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a lender specifies that a borrowed garment is to be pledged for 10 dirhams, but the borrower pledges it for 5 dirhams, what is the ruling according to the text?
A) It is valid and the borrower is not liable because he used it as a pledge.
B) The borrower is liable because part of the garment becomes a trust, harming the lender.
C) The pledge is invalid and the garment must be returned immediately.
D) The lender can only recourse against the borrower for the difference.

Key Takeaway
Borrowing a garment to pledge it is valid in the Hanafi school, but the borrower must adhere to any specifications set by the lender—otherwise, he becomes liable for the garment's value.

Lending an Item for Pledge: General Rule and Specifying the Amount
Ruling on lending for pledge with or without amount specification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a lender lends an item for pledge without conditions, and explain when the borrower becomes liable if the amount is specified.

Core Idea
Absolute permission gives freedom; specifying a limit binds the borrower, and deviation causes liability.

When someone lends a garment to be pawned, the borrower's authority depends on the lender's conditions. The Hanafi school distinguishes between unrestricted permission and specified amounts. This lesson covers the scenarios of no specification and when the amount is defined, including the consequences of pawning for less or more than specified.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the borrower's authority
The text deals with lending an item (thawb) for the purpose of pledging (rahn). First, determine whether the lender imposed any conditions (amount, person, place) or gave absolute permission.
The default ruling is absolute permission unless restricted.
2
Apply the rule for unlimited lending
If the lender does not specify any condition, the borrower may pawn the item for any amount and to any person. The lender's consent is implied because his goal is to have his debt repaid from that property.
Analogy: borrowing an animal without specifying its use gives the borrower full discretion.
3
Analyze the case of specified amount
If the lender names a specific amount (e.g., 10 dirhams), the borrower must adhere. Evaluate the scenarios: pawning for less than specified, more than specified, or when the item's value is less than the named amount.
Key point: deviation from the specification causes liability due to increased harm or risk to the lender.
4
Determine liability based on value and type
If the item's value is equal to or greater than the specified amount, pawning for less harms the lender (partial trust). If pawning for more, redemption becomes difficult. If the item's value is less, pawning for its actual value is allowed, but pawning with a different type (e.g., food instead of dirhams) causes liability.
The lender's purpose is to have recourse in the same type of property (e.g., dirhams).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإذا أعار ثوباً ليرهنه فلا يخلو إما إن لم له شيئاً أو له مالاً أو عين له سمى ولم يسم ما فله يرهنه به متاعاً أو شخصاً، فإن أعار ثوباً ليرهنه وعين له مكاناً أو شخصاً بأي قدر وبأي نوع شاء لأنه طلب منه قضاء دينه من هذا المال مطلقاً لأن الرهن يرهن إيفاء واستيفاء حكماً، ولو طلب منه قضاء دينه من ماله جاز فكذا هذا، والاستعارة ما وجدت مطلقة فقد رضي المعير بأن يرهن بما شاء كما لو استعار من رجل دابة ولم يسم يعمل بها فله أن يركب ويركب غيره ويحمل عليها فكذا هذا. وإذا سمى مالا مقدوراً فرهن بأقل أو أكثر، فإن كانت قيمتهما سواء أو أكثر فرهنه بأقل مما سمى فيتضرر به المعير فإن بعضه يكون أمانة عند المرتهن وهو لم يرض بذلك بل طلب أن يجعل كله مضموناً، وأما إذا رهنه بأكثر فلأنه قد يحتاج المعير إلى الفكاك ليصير إلى ملكه وربما يتعسر عليه الفكاك متى زادت على المسمى لأنه قد لا يجد الزيادة على المسمى فيتضرر به وهو قد رضي بضمان قليل ولم يرض بقضاء دين كثير فصار مخالفاً. وإن كانت قيمة الثوب أقل من المسمى بأن أعار ثوباً ليرهنه بعشرة وقيمته تسعة فإن رهن بقدر قيمته تسعة لا يضمن، وأما إذا رهنه بجنس آخر ضمن في الفصول كلها لأن مقصوده من تسمية الدراهم أن يرجع عليه بالدراهم متى هلك الثوب، ومتى رهن بالطعام لا يمكنه الرجوع عليه بالدراهم، ولأنه ربما يحتاج إلى انفكاك وربما يتيسر له الكفاك بالدراهم ويتعسر عليك الفكاك بالطعام فيلحقه يزادة ضرر. وأما إذا أعاره ليرهنه من إنسان بعينه وفرهنه من غيره ضمن لأنه ربما يحتاج إلى أن يقضي دينه لاستخلاص ملكه والناس يتفاوتون في القضاء والاقتضاء فكذلك في الحفظ والأمانة فالرضا بحفظ زيد لا يكون رضا بحفظ عمرو فالخلاف يخلفه زيادة ضرر. ولو أعاره ليرهنه بالكوفة فرهنه بالبصرة ضمن لأن البلدان والأمكنة متفاوتة في الحفظ والصيانة ولأنه يخاف خطر الطريق متى نقل، ولأنه قد يتيسر له الفكاك في المكان المشروط ويتعسر عليه الفكاك في غيره. وإذا اختلفا في الهلاك أو النقصان قبل الاسترداد من المرتهن أو بعده فالقول للمستعير والبينة للمعير لأنه يدعي قضاء دينه من ينكر.
So if he lends a garment to be pawned, it is either that he has nothing, or he has wealth, or he specified a thing, he named or did not name, so he may pawn it with anything or anyone. If he lends a garment to be pawned and specifies a place or person, then he may pawn it for any amount and any type because he asked him to repay his debt from this property absolutely, because the pawn is pawned for fulfilment and recovery by implication. If he asked him to repay his debt from his property, it is permissible; likewise this. The loan is found absolute, so the lender has consented to pawn with whatever he wishes, just as if he borrowed from a man a riding animal and did not specify what to do with it, then he may ride, let others ride, and load it; similarly this. And if he specifies a defined amount and he pawns for less or more: if the value is equal or more and he pawns for less than specified, he harms the lender because part becomes a trust with the pledgee and he did not consent to that, but rather asked all to be guaranteed. As for if he pawns for more, the lender may need to redeem and perhaps redemption becomes difficult when it exceeds the named amount because he may not find the excess, harming him; he consented to little guarantee and not to much debt, so he has deviated. And if the garment's value is less than specified, e.g., he lends a garment to pawn for ten and its value is nine, then if he pawns for its value nine, he is not liable. But if he pawns for another type, he is liable in all sections because his purpose in naming dirhams is to have recourse for dirhams when the garment is destroyed; when he pawns for food, he cannot have recourse for dirhams. And also because he may need redemption and redemption may be easy with dirhams but difficult with food, causing additional harm. And if he lends him to pawn from a specific person and he pawns from another, he is liable because he may need to repay his debt to extract his property, and people differ in repayment and collection; likewise in preservation and trust. Consent to Zayd's preservation is not consent to 'Amr's, so disagreement causes increased harm. And if he lends him to pawn in Kufa and he pawns in Basra, he is liable because cities and places differ in preservation and care, and because he fears the danger of the road when transferring, and because redemption may be easy in the stipulated place and difficult elsewhere. And if they dispute regarding destruction or deficiency before or after recovery from the pledgee, the word is the borrower's and the proof is the lender's because he claims repayment of his debt from him who denies.
Source pages p. 491

Commentary
This passage is a series of rulings from the chapter on pawn (rahn) in the Hanafi school, specifically regarding a loan (ariyah) of an item for the purpose of pledging it. The text opens the discussion by stating the general rule: when a person lends a garment (or any item) to someone so that the borrower can pawn it, the arrangement falls into several categories. If the lender does not specify any condition (amount, person, or place), the borrower is free to pawn it for any amount and to any person, because the lender's permission is absolute. The passage draws an analogy to borrowing an animal without specifying its use—the borrower may ride it, let others ride, and load it. The key principle is that the lender's goal is to have his debt paid from that property; if he gives absolute permission, he is deemed to accept any arrangement that achieves that goal. However, if the lender specifies a particular amount, and the borrower pawns it for less (while the item's value is equal or more), the borrower becomes liable because part of the pawn becomes a trust (amanah) rather than fully guaranteed, contrary to the lender's intent. If he pawns for more than the specified amount, he also becomes liable because the lender may face difficulty redeeming the extra amount. If the pawned item's value is less than the specified amount (e.g., a garment worth nine pawned for ten), and the borrower only pawns it for its worth (nine), he is not liable. But if he pawns for a different type (e.g., food instead of dirhams), he is liable because the lender intended recourse in dirhams. Similarly, if the lender specifies a particular person or place, the borrower must respect that; otherwise he becomes liable due to increased risk and difficulty. The passage concludes with a rule on disputes about destruction: if the pawn is destroyed or damaged, and the lender claims repayment (i.e., that the borrower had already repaid the debt from the pawn) while the borrower denies, the borrower's word is taken with an oath, and the lender must provide proof. This is because the lender is claiming that the borrower's debt has been satisfied, which the borrower denies. Throughout, the 'illa (effective cause) for liability is the borrower's deviation from the lender's conditions, which increases the lender's harm or risk. The commentary reflects the Hanafi school's reliance on istihsan and detailed analysis of consent.

Key Terms
عارية (ariyah): A loan of property for use without compensation, specifically here for the purpose of pledging.
رهن (rahn): A pledge or pawn, where property is held as security for a debt.
معير (mu'ir): The lender of the item (the owner who allows it to be pawned).
مستعير (musta'ir): The borrower of the item, who then pledges it.
مرتهن (murtahin): The creditor who receives the pawn.
فكاك (fakak): Redemption of the pawn by paying off the debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The borrower is not liable because the debt is less.
B) The borrower is liable because he deviated from the specification.
C) The borrower is liable only if the garment is destroyed.
D) The borrower is not liable because the lender's rights are still protected.

Key Takeaway
The borrower must adhere to the lender's specifications; any deviation causing increased harm or altering the guarantee renders the borrower liable.

Liability of the Borrower in Pawn of Borrowed Items
Rulings on borrower liability and disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions that make the borrower of a pawn liable and apply them to scenarios of deviation and repayment.

Core Idea
The borrower of a pawn is liable only if he deviates from conditions or uses the pawn to repay his own debt.

In this lesson, we examine the liability of the musta'ir (borrower) in 'ariyah for rahn. The Hanafi school establishes clear rules: the borrower is a trustee (amin) until he deviates or uses the pawn to repay his own debt. We will work through several case studies to apply these principles, including disputes between pledgor and lender, perishing in the borrower's hand, and scenarios involving agents and repentance from deviation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and their roles
Note the pledgor (raahin), the pledgee (murtahin), the lender (mu'ir), and the borrower (musta'ir). Understand that the musta'ir holds the pawn as a trust (amanah) on behalf of the pledgor.
2
Identify the two causes of liability for the borrower
From the text: 'al-musta'ir innama yadmanu bi-ahaday amrayn: imma bil-khilaf aw bi-an yaqdi daynahu minhu'. The borrower is liable only if he deviates from the lender's conditions or uses the pawn to repay his own debt.
Deviation (khilaf) means pawning to a different person or for a different amount than agreed.
3
Apply to the dispute scenario (pledgor claims borrower recovered before redemption)
If the pledgor and pledgee agree that the borrower recovered the pawn before redemption, the pledgor is believed. The lender then claims repayment from the pawn, but the pledgor denies; the pledgor's word is taken, and the lender can recoup from the pledgor. Here, the borrower is not liable because neither deviation nor using for debt occurred.
4
Apply to the agent scenario (borrower hands pawn to agent of pledgor)
If the pledgor repays his debt and sends an agent to collect the pawn, and the pawn perishes in the agent's hand, the borrower is liable unless the agent is from the borrower's household (like a depositee). This is because delivering to a stranger without owner's permission is a deviation.
The borrower may lend the pawn to a stranger but may not deposit it with a stranger outside his household.
5
Apply to the riding-and-redeeming scenario
The borrower rides the borrowed animal before pawning (deviation), then pawns it, then repays the debt, but the animal perishes with the pledgee. The borrower is not liable because he returned to compliance (al-ittifaq) after deviation, thereby restoring his trustee status.
The principle: deviation can be cured by returning to compliance before the loss.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن ادعى الراهن أن المستعير استرد الرهن قبل الافتكاك وصدقه المرتهن يصدق الراهن لأن الراهن والمرتهن تصادقا على فسخ الرهن والرهن عقد جرى بينهما فيكون ماله والقول وقولهما أنهما فسخا ذلك كما في المتبايعين لأن المعير ادعى أنه قضى دينه من وأنكر الراهن فيكون القول قوله ويرجع المعير على الراهن بقدر ما يذهب عنه بالدين لأنه قد صار قاضياً دينه من ماله بهذا القدر بأمره، فإذا هلك عند المستعير قبل الرهن أو بعد ماله والمستعير بالإعارة، ومن هذا عن ماله الفكاك لا يضمن لأن المستعير إنما يضمن العارية بأحد أمرين : إما بالخلاف أو بأن يقضي دينه منه ولم يوجد أحدهما فأما لا يضمن بالقبض والدفع إلى المرتهن لأنه حصل بإذن المالك. قضى الراهن دينه وبعث وكيلاً يقبض العبد فهلك في يد الوكيل ضمن المستعير إلا أن يكون من عياله كالمودع وهذه تدل على أن المستعير ليس له أن يودع من ليس في عياله وإن كان له أن يعير من ليس في عياله، وفي الحالين دفع الأمانة إلى من ليس في عياله وذلك لأن الدفع إلى الأجنبي في العارية إنما حصل بإذن المالك لأن المعير ملك المنفعة ملك المنفعة بغير بدل لم يملك المنفعة بالوديعة ليحصل له الإذن تبعاً لتملك المنفعة رهن المستعار بألف وقيمته ألف ولم يقبض المال فهلك في يد المرتهن فعلى الراهن ألف للمعير وعلى المرتهن ألف للراهن لأن المقبوض على سوم الرهن مضمون على القابض كالمقبوض بحقيقة الرهن فضمن المرتهن مثل المسمى هو ألف للراهن، وما أخذ من المرتهن بدل العبد فيكون لمالك العبد من حيث إنه بدل ملكه لا من حيث إنه قضى دينه من فإنه لم يكن عليه دين للمرتهن استعار من رجلين متاعاً للرهن ثم قضى نصف المال وقال نصیب فلان يكون عنهما لأن كل جزء من أجزاء الرهن محبوس بجميع الدين إذ لو جعلنا كل جزء محبوساً ببعض الدين يمكن الشيوع في الرهن وأنه يوجب بطلان الرهن فلا يمكن أن يجعل البعض محبوساً ببعض الدين، فلهذا لو قضى كان ما قضى عن جميع العبد. رهن المستعار بألف وقيمته ألف فقضى الدين وهلك في يد المرتهن فالمرتهن ضامن الألف يردها على مولى العبد ولا ضمان للمعير على الراهن، وفي رواية أبي حفص ردها على الراهن وردها الراهن على المعير وهو الصحيح لأن المعير صار قاضياً دينه بهلاك الراهن من وقت الارتهان لأنه صار مستوفياً للدين في حق مل اليد والحبس من وقت القبض فظهر أنه استوفى منه الألف وليس عليه دين ولم يكن له حق الاستيفاء فوجب على المرتهن ردها على الراهن لأنه استوفاها منه، ثم يردها على مولى العبد لأنه قضى دينه من ماله بأمره. قبض دابة عارية ليرهنها فركبها ثم رهنها ثم قضى المال ولم يقبض الرهن حتى هلكت عند المرتهن لا ضمان على الراهن لأنه المستعير للرهن مودع خالف بالركوب وقد عاد إلى الوفاق فيبرأ عن الضمان وفي الجامع : أصله أن القاضي نصب لإيفاء الحقوق المحترمة إلى أربابها لا لإبطالها وإهدارها مات المعير والمستعير لم يكن للورثة الاسترداد لأن فيه إزالة يده وإبطال ,حقه ولو كان على المعير دين ولا مال له سواه وفيه فضل عن دين المستعير لم يبع حتى يجتمع الغرماء والورثة لأن أباهم يكون مفيداً لأنه متى لم يبع الرهن ربما يقضي المستعير دين نفسه أو يبرئه المرتهن عن دينه فيسلم الرهن لهم فيبيعون ويقضون حق غريم المعير ويبقى الفضل لهم، ولو بيع بغير رضاهم ربما لا يصل إليهم شيء أو في
If the pledgor claims that the borrower recovered the pawn before redemption and the pledgee confirms him, the pledgor is believed because the pledgor and pledgee have mutually agreed on the annulment of the pawn, and the pawn is a contract between them, so it is their word that they have annulled it, as in the case of buyer and seller, because the lender claimed that he repaid his debt from it and the pledgor denies, so the word is the pledgor's, and the lender recovers from the pledgor the amount that was discharged from his debt, because he has become a repayer of his debt from his property by his command. So if it perishes in the possession of the borrower before the pawn or after, his property and the borrower with the loan, and from this, concerning his property, redemption is not liable because the borrower is only liable in the loan by one of two things: either by deviation or by repaying his debt from it, and neither occurred, so he is not liable by taking possession and delivering to the pledgee because that occurred with the owner's permission. The pledgor repaid his debt and sent an agent to receive the slave, and it perished in the agent's hand; the borrower is liable unless the agent is from his family like a depositee. This indicates that the borrower may not deposit with one not in his family, although he may lend to one not in his family; in both cases it is delivering a trust to one not in his family, because the delivery to a stranger in the loan occurred with the owner's permission because the lender owns the usufruct without compensation, he does not own the usufruct by deposit such that permission follows ownership of usufruct. The borrowed item was pawned for one thousand and its value is one thousand, and he did not receive the money, and it perished in the pledgee's hand; then the pledgor owes one thousand to the lender and the pledgee owes one thousand to the pledgor, because what is taken on the basis of a pawn is guaranteed by the taker like what is taken by actual pawn, so the pledgee guarantees the equivalent of the named amount, i.e., one thousand, to the pledgor. And what is taken from the pledgee as compensation for the slave becomes the property of the slave's owner insofar as it is compensation for his property, not insofar as it repays his debt, because he had no debt to the pledgee. He borrowed from two men an item for pawn, then repaid half the money and said: 'the share of so-and-so is from both,' because every part of the pawn is held for the entire debt; if we made each part held for part of the debt, fragmentation would occur in the pawn and that would invalidate the pawn, so it cannot be that part is held for part of the debt. Hence, if he repaid, what he repaid is for the entire slave. The borrowed item was pawned for one thousand and its value is one thousand; he repaid the debt and it perished in the pledgee's hand; then the pledgee guarantees the one thousand, returning it to the owner of the slave, and no liability of the lender against the pledgor. In the narration of Abu Hafs, he returns it to the pledgor, and the pledgor returns it to the lender, and this is correct, because the lender became a repayer of his debt by the destruction of the pledgor from the time of pawn because he became a receiver of the debt in terms of hand and possession from the time of taking possession; so it appears that he received from him the one thousand, and he has no debt, and he had no right of receipt, so it is obligatory for the pledgee to return it to the pledgor because he received it from him, then he returns it to the owner of the slave because he repaid his debt from his property by his command. He took possession of an animal as a loan to pawn it; he rode it, then pawned it, then repaid the money, and did not receive the pawn until it perished with the pledgee; there is no liability on the pledgor because the borrower for the pawn is a depositee who deviated by riding but returned to compliance, so he is discharged from liability. And in al-Jami': its basis is that the judge is appointed to deliver respected rights to their owners, not to invalidate and waste them. The lender and borrower died; the heirs may not recover because that would remove his hand and invalidate his right. And if the lender has a debt and has no property other than it, and there is a surplus over the borrower's debt, it is not sold until the creditors and heirs gather, because their father would be beneficial, because when the pawn is not sold, perhaps the borrower will repay his own debt or the pledgee will release him from his debt, so the pawn is saved for them, and they sell it and pay the right of the lender's creditor, and the surplus remains for them. And if it were sold without their consent, perhaps nothing would reach them or...
Source pages p. 491

Commentary
This passage continues the rulings on 'ariyah for rahn, addressing several complex scenarios. First, it discusses a dispute: if the pledgor (the original debtor) claims that the borrower (musta'ir) recovered the pawn before redemption, and the pledgee confirms this, the pledgor is believed because both parties to the pawn contract have agreed on its annulment. The lender (mu'ir) then claims that his debt was repaid from the pawn, but the pledgor denies; the pledgor's word is taken, and the lender can claim reimbursement from the pledgor for the amount of debt discharged. If the pawn perishes with the borrower before or after pawning, the borrower is not liable because he has not deviated nor used the pawn to repay his own debt. Next, a scenario: the pledgor repays his debt and sends an agent to collect the pawned slave; the slave perishes in the agent's hand; the borrower is liable unless the agent is part of his household (like a depositee). This illustrates that the borrower cannot entrust the pawn to a stranger, though he can lend it to a stranger. The passage then covers a case where the borrowed item is pawned for its exact value but the money is not received (i.e., the pledgee does not pay the debt to the pledgor? Actually, the text says 'lam yaqbid al-mal' meaning the pledgee did not receive the debt? Or the pledgor did not receive the loan? Need careful reading. The Hanafi position: the pawn is guaranteed by the pledgee; if it perishes, the pledgee owes its value. Another case: a man borrows from two people to pawn, then repays half the debt; the repayment is applied to the entire pawn because each part is held for the entire debt; partial repayment does not release any specific part—a key Hanafi principle to avoid shuyu' (undivided share) which invalidates pawn. Then, if the pawn is redeemed and then perishes with the pledgee, the pledgee pays its value. There is an ikhtilaf: according to the correct narration from Abu Hafs, the pledgee pays the pledgor, who then pays the lender. The passage ends with a ruling from al-Jami' about the purpose of the judge, and a case where the lender and borrower die; the heirs cannot unilaterally recover the pawn. If the lender has debts and the pawn has surplus value, it is not sold until all creditors and heirs gather, to preserve potential benefit for the heirs. The final sentence is cut off. This passage demonstrates the meticulous casuistry of Hanafi fiqh, applying principles of guarantee, trust, deviation, and consent.

Key Terms
افتكاك (iftikak): Redemption of the pawn by paying the debt.
الخلف (al-khilaf): Deviation from the lender's conditions (e.g., pawning to a different person or for a different amount)
المودع (al-mudi'): A depositee; one with whom property is left for safekeeping.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A borrower deviates by using the pawned item for his own business without permission, but then returns it to the pledgee. The item is later destroyed by fire. Is the borrower liable?
A) Yes, because the deviation was not cured
B) Yes, because the borrower is always liable for loss
C) No, because the borrower returned to compliance before loss
D) No, because fire is an act of God

Key Takeaway
The borrower of a pawn is liable only for deviation from conditions or using the pawn to repay his own debt; returning to compliance removes liability.
