The Hanafi school distinguishes between injury by animals (jubar) and by slaves (liability), with proportional debt transfer in complex cases.

Separate Pledges: Injury and Ransom Options for Pawned Slaves
Rulings on pawned slaves in separate pledges with mutual injury and ransom.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi options available when a pawned slave injures another in a separate pledge and identify the intra-Hanafi difference on liability for ransom by the mortgagee.

Core Idea
In separate pledges, each slave stands alone; the pawner and mortgagee share an option to ransom or replace.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses the rules when two pawned slaves, each securing a separate debt, injure each other. The central concept is that because the pledges are separate, the rights of the mortgagee attach individually, giving both parties a choice (khayar) to either swap the offending slave for the victim or pay compensation. We will also examine the special case where the mortgagee ransoms while the pawner is absent, which splits the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and presence of surplus
Determine that two slaves are pawned separately (each for 500). If one kills the other, check if total value equals the debt (no surplus). If no surplus, the debt on the slain falls. If surplus exists, proceed to options.
Surplus means the total value exceeds total debt.
2
Apply the option (khayar) between replacement and ransom
If surplus exists, the pawner and mortgagee may either: (a) make the killer take the slain's place, voiding the slain's debt; or (b) ransom the killer by paying the slain's value (500 each), making that value a new pawn. The killer remains a pawn.
Part injury (blinding) follows the same choice, with ransom based on the arsh (compensation for the part).
3
Reason through the rationale
Because the transactions are separate, each slave is 'empty' of the other's debt. Thus, the injury is like injury to a stranger's slave, giving the same option. The ransom is split equally between pawner and mortgagee because half of the killer is guaranteed against the mortgagee.
The reasoning (talil) emphasizes independence of pledges.
4
Analyse the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on voluntary ransom
If the mortgagee ransoms while the pawner is absent, Abu Hanifa holds the pawner owes half the ransom (debt). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say the mortgagee is a volunteer (mutabarri'), so no reimbursement. The text notes the ikhtilaf but does not resolve it here.
The dispute hinges on whether the mortgagee acts to preserve his own interest or the pawner's.
5
Handle self-injury and complex cases
Self-injury (suicide or self-blinding) is void – no liability – like natural death. For two female slaves with offspring, the debt is not divided equally because values are equal; each slave is considered partly empty and partly occupied.
The ruling on self-injury is absolute: a person's injury to himself is legally disregarded.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما إذا ارتهن عبدين كل واحد بخمسمائة بصفقة على حدة فقتل أحدهما صاحبه، فإن لم يكن فيهما فضل عن الدين روي عن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله أنه يسقط ما في المجني عليه لأنه لا فائدة في الدفع للمرتهن وهدرت ،الجناية فإن كان فيهما فضل يخير الراهن والمرتهن إن شاء جعلا القاتل مكان المقتول وبطل ما في المقتول من الدين، وإن شاء أفديا القاتل بقيمة المقتول وغرم كل واحد خمسمائة فكانت القيمة رهناً مكان المقتول. والقاتل رهن بحاله لأن المقتول كله تلف بجناية الفارغ لأن الصفقة متى تفرقت فالحق المتعلق بأحدهما لا يتعلق بالآخر فكان كل واحد منهما فارغاً عن الآخر، ولهذا لو قضى دين أحدهما كان له أن يفتكه وجناية المشغول على الفارغ معتبرة فصار كما لو جنى أحدهما على عبد لأجنبي يخير الراهن والمرتهن بين الدفع والفداء فكذا هذا وإن اختار الفداء فكذا هذا. وإن اختار الفداء غرم كل واحد خمسمائة لأن نصف القاتل مضمون على المرتهن وعبده أمانة عنده فكان الفداء عليهما اعتباراً للبعض بالكل، وإن كان فقأ أحدهما عين الآخر فقيل لهما ادفعاه أو افدياه بأرش عليه الآخر لأن إتلاف البعض يعتبر بإتلاف الكل، وفي إتلاف الكل يخير فكذا في إتلاف البعض، فإن دفعه بطل ما فيه من الدين، وإن فدياه كان الفداء عليهما نصفين رهناً مع المفقوءة عينه. ولو قال المرتهن لا أفدي وادع الرهن على حاله له ذلك والمفقوءة عينه ذهب نصف باقية لأن هذه الجناية إنما تعتبر لحق المرتهن لا لحق الراهن لأنه لو طلب الجناية ودفع الجاني سقط نصف الدين ولو ترك الجناية يسقط الدين فكان ربع في طلب الجناية ضرر بالمرتهن، فإذا رضي بإبطال حقه فله ذلك ويسقط اعتبار الجناية، ولو قال الراهن افديه وقال المرتهن لا أفديه للراهن أن يفديه بأرش الجناية كلها لأنه محتاج إلى الفداء ليخلص عبد الرهن عند الجناية، فإن فداه يكون له نصف ذلك عما على المرتهن في العبد الجاني ويبطل في حقه من العبد الجاني نصفه لأن الرهن مضطر إلى الفداء يحيي ملكه والإنسان فيما يحيي ملكه لا يكون متبرعاً فيكون له حق الرجوع عليه وللمرتهن عليه مثله فيلتقيان قصاصاً فيصير مؤدياً دين القاتل فيخرج القاتل من الرهن وإن أبى الراهن الفداء وقال المرتهن أفدي وفدى يكون متطوعاً فيه إذا كان الراهن حاضراً لأن بقدر المضمون أدى . عن نفسه وبقدر الأمانة أدى عن الراهن وهو غير مضطر فيه لأنه غير محيي ملكه فيكون متبرع رعاً. وإن كان الراهن غائباً كان على الراهن نصف الفداء ديناً، قيل هذا عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى، وعندهما يكون متبرعاً كان الراهن حاضراً أو غائباً لما يأتي. ولو قتل العبد المرهون نفسه أو فقأ عينه فلا شيء عليه كما لو مات لأن جناية الإنسان على نفسه هدر لما تبين إذا كان الرهن أمتين قيمة كل واحدة ألف فولدت كل واحدة تساوي ألفاً والدين ألف فقتلت إحدى البنتين صاحبتها لم يبطل من الدين شيء والباقي رهن بألف كلها لأن الدين لم ينقسم عليهما وعلى ولديهما أرباعاً على سبيل الترقب والانتظار لأن قيمتهما على السواء فصارت كل واحدة فارغة وربعها مشغول
And as for when he pawns two slaves, each for five hundred, in separate transactions, and one kills his companion: then if there is no surplus in them over the debt [i.e., total value equals debt], it is narrated from Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, that what is [secured] in the slain one falls because there is no benefit in payment for the mortgagee (mortgagee), and the injury is void. But if there is a surplus, the pawner and mortgagee have an option: if they wish, they make the killer take the place of the killed, and the debt in the killed becomes void; and if they wish, they ransom the killer by the value of the killed, and each pays five hundred, so the value becomes a pawn in place of the killed. The killer remains a pawn as he was, because the killed [slave] perished entirely by the injury of the empty [slave] – because when the transactions are separate, the right attached to one does not attach to the other, so each of them is empty with respect to the other. Hence if he paid off the debt of one of them, he could redeem him. And the injury of the occupied against the empty is considered. So it is as if one of them injured a slave belonging to a stranger: the pawner and mortgagee have the option between handing over and ransoming. Likewise this. And if they choose ransom, each pays five hundred, because half of the killer is guaranteed against the mortgagee and his slave is an amanah (trust) with him, so the ransom is upon both, considering the part as the whole. And if one of them blinded the eye of the other, it is said to them: hand him over [to the victim] or ransom him with the arsh (compensation) upon the other, because the destruction of a part is considered like the destruction of the whole, and in the destruction of the whole they are given the option, so likewise in the destruction of the part. If they hand him over, the debt in him becomes void; and if they ransom him, the ransom is upon them half each, as a pawn along with the one whose eye was blinded. And if the mortgagee says, 'I will not ransom, and let the pawn remain as it is,' he has that right, and the one whose eye was blinded loses half [of his value] remaining? [؟] because this injury is considered only for the right of the mortgagee, not for the right of the pawner. Because if he claims the injury and hands over the injurer, half the debt falls; and if he abandons the claim, the debt does not fall? [؟] So a quarter in claiming the injury is a loss for the mortgagee. So if he consents to invalidate his right, he may do so, and the consideration of the injury falls. And if the pawner says, 'I will ransom,' and the mortgagee says, 'I will not ransom,' then the pawner may ransom him with the full arsh because he needs the ransom to free the pawned slave upon the injury. Then if he ransoms him, he will have half of that against what the mortgagee owes in the offending slave, and from his right in the offending slave half becomes void, because the pawner is compelled to ransom to revive his property, and a person in reviving his property is not a volunteer (mutabarri'). So he has a right of recourse against him, and the mortgagee has the like against him, so they meet as retaliation (qisas) [setoff], and he becomes as if he paid the debt of the killer, so the killer exits from the pawn. And if the pawner refuses the ransom and the mortgagee says 'I will ransom' and ransoms, he is a volunteer therein if the pawner is present, because to the extent of the guaranteed [portion] he paid for himself, and to the extent of the trust he paid for the pawner, and he is not compelled therein because he is not reviving his own property, so he is a volunteer. And if the pawner is absent, then half of the ransom is a debt upon the pawner. It is said that this is according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah Almighty have mercy on him. But according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he would be a volunteer whether the pawner is present or absent, as will come. And if a pawned slave kills himself or blinds his own eye, nothing is upon him, just as if he died, because a person's injury to himself is void. This is clarified when the pawned [slaves] are two female slaves, each worth one thousand, and they give birth – each [child] is worth one thousand, and the debt is one thousand – and one of the daughters kills her companion: nothing becomes void of the debt, and the remaining [slave] is a pawn for the entire thousand because the debt is not divided among them and their offspring in quarters on the basis of anticipation and waiting because their values are equal. So each becomes empty [؟] and a quarter of her is occupied.
Source pages p. 502

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq covers several situations involving pawned slaves in separate pledges. First, the case where two slaves are each pawned for a separate debt (500 each) in separate transactions. If one kills the other, and the total value of both slaves equals the debt (no surplus), Abu Hanifa ruled that the debt secured by the slain slave falls, as the mortgagee gains no benefit from the transaction. But if there is a surplus, the pawner and mortgagee have an option: either to replace the killed with the killer (so the killer's value secures the debt), or to ransom the killer by paying the value of the killed, and that value becomes the new pawn. The reasoning: in separate pledges, each slave is 'empty' with respect to the other's debt, so injury is like injury to a slave owned by a third party, giving the option. The same option applies to blinding (injury of a part). If the mortgagee refuses to ransom, he may leave the pawn as is, and the injury is disregarded. If the pawner ransoms, he can recover half from the mortgagee. An intra-Hanafi dispute arises: if the mortgagee ransoms while the pawner is absent, Abu Hanifa says the pawner owes half the ransom, but Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say the mortgagee is a volunteer. The passage then covers self-injury (suicide or self-blinding): it is void, no liability, because a person's injury to himself is legally disregarded. Finally, a case involving two pawned female slaves with their offspring: despite the complication, the debt remains undivided because the values are equal, and each is considered partly empty and partly occupied.

Key Terms
صفقة على حدة (safqatun 'ala hidatin): Separate transactions; each slave is pledged independently for its own debt.
فداء (fida'): Ransom; payment made to redeem the offending pawned slave from liability for injury.
متبرع (mutabarri'): A volunteer; one who acts without compulsion and without expectation of reimbursement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In separate pledges, if one pawned slave kills the other and there is a surplus in value, what are the options for the pawner and mortgagee?
A) They must sell both slaves.
B) They can either replace the killer or ransom him.
C) The debt is automatically divided equally.
D) The mortgagee alone decides.

Key Takeaway
In separate pledges, the pawner and mortgagee share an option to replace or ransom, but self-injury is void, and an intra-Hanafi dispute exists on volunteer ransom.

Self-Injury by a Mortgaged Slave Is Legally Null
States a ruling with a brief analogy and principle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a mortgaged slave’s self-injury and explain the underlying principle that self-injury is legally disregarded.

Core Idea
A person's injury against himself is null; no liability arises from self-harm.

This passage presents a concise but important principle in the law of mortgage (rahn): when a mortgaged slave harms himself, there is no compensation claim. The result follows from the broader Hanafi rule that self-injury is inherently null (hadar). Understanding this helps distinguish cases where the slave harms a third party versus himself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is a mortgaged slave killing himself or gouging out his own eye. The ruling: nothing is due upon him (لا شيء عليه).
2
Recognise the analogy
The author analogises to natural death: just as death ends liability, self-injury extinguishes any claim.
The Arabic says 'كما لو مات' – just as if he died.
3
State the underlying principle
The maxim: جناية الإنسان على نفسه هدر (a person’s injury against himself is of no legal effect).
This principle applies universally, not only in mortgage.
4
Apply to the mortgage
The mortgagee’s claim remains only on the slave’s remaining value; no separate compensation is due from the slave or his estate.
If the slave dies, the mortgagee’s claim is only against the estate, but no additional penalty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قتل العبد المرهون نفسه أو فقأ عينه فلا شيء عليه كما لو مات لأن جناية الإنسان على نفسه هدر
If the mortgaged slave kills himself or gouges out his own eye, nothing is due upon him, just as if he died, because a person's injury against himself is null.
Source pages p. 502

Commentary
This is a short ruling establishing that self-injury by a mortgaged slave does not affect the mortgage or create liability. It is analogous to natural death: the claim of the mortgagee remains only on the remaining value of the slave. The principle is that a person cannot claim compensation from himself.

Key Terms
هدر (hadar): Null; of no legal effect or consequence

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The debt is reduced proportionally.
B) The debt becomes void.
C) The debt remains unaffected, and the slave must be ransomed.
D) The debt remains unaffected.

Key Takeaway
Self-injury by a mortgaged slave is legally null (hadar); no compensation arises and the mortgage is unaffected.

Ruling When Offspring of Two Mortgaged Female Slaves Kills Each Other
Detailed calculation of debt when one daughter kills the other

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the new encumbrance of a pawned slave after an injury, applying the Hanafi principle of taraqqub wa intizār.

Core Idea
In multi-pawn debts, encumbrance is proportional and shifts upon injury, not fixed in advance.

This lesson explores a classic Hanafi scenario involving two female slaves pawned for a single debt, each with a daughter of equal value. When one daughter kills the other, the debt is not simply divided equally; instead, the encumbrance shifts according to the principle of taraqqub wa intizār (anticipation and waiting). Understanding this calculation is essential for a mufti dealing with complex pawn transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and assets
List all pawned items: two female slaves (each worth 1000), each with a daughter (worth 1000). Total pawn value 4000. Debt is 1000. One daughter kills the other.
The debt is 1000, which is less than total pawn value, so each item is partially encumbered.
2
Understand taraqqub wa intizār
The debt does not divide into fixed quarters among the four slaves. Instead, it attaches proportionally to each slave's value, but the exact distribution is 'in anticipation' because the offspring are considered extensions of the mothers.
This means each slave (mother and her daughter) is treated as a unit with the mother's original pawn status.
3
Determine vacant and encumbered portions
Each female slave (value 1000) has a debt share of 250 (since total debt 1000 across 4000 value = 1/4). So each mother is 1/4 encumbered (250) and 3/4 vacant (750). Her daughter is also 1/4 encumbered via the mother's pawn status.
Thus each of the four individuals is 1/4 encumbered? Actually, the text says each female slave (the mother) becomes 1/4 encumbered, but the daughter inherits that encumbrance proportionally. The calculation treats the mother and daughter as a unit.
4
Apply injury rules
The slain daughter has three quarters vacant (750) and one quarter encumbered (250). The injury on the three vacant quarters is disregarded (telf bi-jinayat al-farigh 'ala al-farigh). The injury on the three-quarters of the encumbered quarter (i.e., 3/4 of 250 = 187.5) is considered because it is injury of vacant upon encumbered, so the debt shifts to the killer.
The killer daughter now bears the slain's encumbrance plus her own, totaling 750? Let's calculate: killer was initially 250 encumbered; plus 250 from slain? Actually text says killer becomes 750.
5
Calculate final encumbrance of killer
The killer daughter was originally encumbered with 250 (her share). After the killing, she becomes encumbered with an additional 500 (the shifted debt from the slain), totaling 750. If the mother of the slain dies, further adjustment yields 787.5.
The text ends with 'and she ransoms herself with that', meaning the killer's pawn value is now 750, and she can be redeemed by paying that amount.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا كان الرهن أمتين قيمة كل واحدة ألف فولدت كل واحدة تساوي ألفاً والدين ألف فقتلت إحدى البنتين صاحبتها لم يبطل من الدين شيء والباقي رهن بألف كلها لأن الدين لم ينقسم عليهما وعلى ولديهما أرباعاً على سبيل الترقب والانتظار لأن قيمتهما على السواء فصارت كل واحدة فارغة وربعها مشغول بالألف بالدين لأن قيمة كل واحدة مثل الدين والمقتولة ثلاثة أرباعها فارغة وربعها مشغول والجناية على ثلاثة أرباعها هدر لأنه تلف بجناية الفارغ على الفارغ وبجناية المشغول على الفارغ إلا أنه لا يسقط ما بإزائه من الدين ولكن يلحق باقيها لأن بفوات الدين يتحول ما فيه من الدين إلى الأم والجناية على ثلاثة أرباع ربع المشغول معتبرة لأنه تلف بجناية الفارغ على المشغول فتحول ما بإزائه من الدين على القاتلة فصارت القاتلة رهناً بسبعمائة وخمسين. وأما القاتلة كانت رهناً بمائتين وخمسين وذلك كله ألف إن ماتت أم المقتولة بقيت القاتلة وأمها بسبعمائة وسبعة وثمانين ونصف لحقها من الجناية وافتكها بذلك.
And if the pawn consists of two female slaves each worth one thousand, and each gives birth to a daughter worth one thousand, and the debt is one thousand, and one of the daughters kills the other: nothing of the debt is void, and the remaining is a pawn for the full thousand. Because the debt does not divide upon them and their offspring in quarters on the basis of anticipation and expectation, as their values are equal. So each female slave becomes vacant and one quarter of her is encumbered with the debt. Because the value of each is like the debt, and the slain has three quarters vacant and one quarter encumbered. The injury upon three quarters is disregarded because it is loss due to injury of the vacant upon vacant, and due to injury of the encumbered upon vacant, except that it does not drop what is against it from the debt, but it attaches to the remainder. Because by the loss of the debt, what was upon it of debt transfers to the mother. And the injury upon three quarters of the quarter of the encumbered is considered because it is loss due to injury of the vacant upon encumbered, so what was against it of debt transfers to the killer. So the killer becomes a pawn for seven hundred and fifty. And the killer was a pawn for two hundred and fifty, and that is all one thousand. If the mother of the slain dies, the killer and her mother remain at seven hundred and eighty-seven and a half, which attaches to her from the injury, and she ransoms herself with that.
Source pages p. 502

Commentary
This is a complex ruling on a scenario with two mortgaged female slaves (أمتين) each worth 1000, each producing a daughter worth 1000, total debt 1000. One daughter kills the other. The passage first explains that the debt is not divided equally among all four (two mothers and two daughters) because some are not yet in existence? Actually, the reasoning is that the debt is divided across the slave and her offspring proportionally based on each slave's value relative to the debt. Since each female slave is worth 1000 (like the debt), only one quarter of each is actually 'encumbered' (مشغول) because the debt is 1000 and total value is 4000 (each of the four is 1000). However, the text says the debt does not divide into quarters because the offspring are not yet subject to the debt? Actually, the text says 'على سبيل الترقب والانتظار' meaning the debt's division is not fixed but potential. The calculation shows that the killer daughter becomes a pawn for 750, and the slain daughter's mother transfers her encumbrance. If the mother dies, further adjustment occurs. This is a classic Hanafi exercise in distributing debt upon injury among multiple pawned items.

Key Terms
ترقب وانتظار (taraqqub wa intizār): The debt is not fixedly divided but subject to expectation and waiting
فارغة (fārigha): Portion of a slave's value not encumbered by debt

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 750
B) 250
C) 500
D) 1000

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi pawn law, debt is not fixedly divided among multiple pawned items; it is subject to anticipation and waiting (taraqqub wa intizār), and encumbrance may shift upon injury to maintain the debtor's security.

The Substitute Pawn: Muhammad vs. Abu Yusuf on Blinking and Replacement
Intra-Hanafi dispute on substitution in pawn contracts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf regarding the substitution of a pawn after injury, and state the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) for the debt.

Core Idea
A substitute pawn does not fully replace the original; the original reverts and the debt reduces for deficiency.

In the Hanafi school, the contract of pawn (rahn) secures a debt by placing an asset in the mortgagee's possession. When that asset injures someone, it may be surrendered as compensation. But what happens if the pawn itself is later injured? This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq reveals a subtle intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf on whether a substitute fully replaces the original pawn or whether the original retains its status.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
First, understand the factual situation: a mortgaged female slave (ama) worth 1000 with a debt of 1000 gives birth to a son also worth 1000. The son injures a third party and is surrendered as compensation. Later, the mother (original pawn) blinds the daughter (another offspring?). The question: when the mother is eventually returned after injury, does she revert to being the pawn, or does the substitute (the daughter) remain the pawn?
The daughter is also a substitute from an earlier injury? The text is complex; focus on the substitution principle.
2
State Muhammad's position
Imam Muhammad holds that the original pawn (the mother) reverts to its original status upon return. The substitute is disregarded. Consequently, the debt is reduced by the deficiency caused by the injury (e.g., the loss of the mother's eyes).
Muhammad's reasoning: the substitute is a mere follower (tabiʿ); making the followed a follower of its own follower violates legal principles.
3
State Abu Yusuf's position
Abu Yusuf holds that the substitute fully stands in place of the original. When the original is handed over for the substitute, the substitute becomes the pawn. Thus, if the original is later returned, it does not reclaim its pawn status; the debt remains unchanged.
Abu Yusuf's reasoning: the substitute completely replaces the original in all respects.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Under Muhammad, if the mother is later injured, the debt is reduced by the deficiency. Under Abu Yusuf, the debt remains full because the mother is no longer the pawn.
This affects the mortgagee's security and the amount recoverable.
5
Note the tarjih (preferred view)
The passage presents both views. The author of Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq seems to lean towards istihsan, which supports Muhammad's view. However, in the Hanafi school, the view of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is often relied upon if they agree. Here they disagree, so further tarjih is needed from later authorities.
For fatwa purposes, one should check later works like Radd al-Muhtar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أمة مرهونة بألف وقيمتها ألف فولدت ولداً يساوي ألفاً فجنى الولد فدفع بها لم تبطل من الدين شيء لأن دفع الولد بمنزلة الهلاك، ولو هلك الولد لا يسقط شيء من الدين فكذا هذا وإن فقأت الأم عيني البنت فدفعت الأم وأخذت البنت فهي رهن بألف كاملة لأن الأم إن ماتت مات عندهما، وعند محمد رحمه الله تعالى يسقط من الدين بقدر نقصان العين لأن عنده في الجثة العمياء إذا اختار مولى الفاقئ الدفع وأخذ الجثة له ذلك، وليس لمولى المفقوءة إمساك الجثة يضمن النقصان، وكذلك عند أبي يوسف رحمه الله تعالى إذا اختار مولى المفقوءة دفع الجثة وأخذ الفاقئ فالرهن كله فات إلى خلف فيقوم الخلف مقامه وعند محمد رحمه الله تعالى لمولى المفقوءة إمساك الجثة ويضمن النقصان وكان الفاقئ بدلاً عن الجثة وعن العينين جميعاً فما بإزاء العينين من الرهن قد بطل لأن العينين لم تصر ملكاً للراهن ولا وصل إلى المرتهن فكان الرهن بقدر الجثة فائتاً بخلف فيكون رهناً به، فإن فقأت الأم بعد ذلك عيني البنت فدفعت وأخذت الأم عمياء ففي القياس تكون رهناً بجميع المال لأن البنت قامت مقام الأم بالدفع كما قامت الأم مقام البنت بالدفع في جميع الرهن. وفي الاستحسان يعود الرهن الأول على حاله ويذهب منه بحساب ما نقص من العينين لأن الأم كانت أصلاً في الرهن والبنت جعلت بدلاً عنها وتبعاً لها، فإذا دفعت الأم بالبنت فقد وقعت القدرة على الأصل قبل حصول المقصود بالبلد لأن المقصود من الرهن الإيفاء ولم يوجد الإيفاء فسقط اعتبار البدل فبقيت الأم أصلاً في الرهن كما كانت قبل الدفع لا بدلاً عن البنت فكانت أصلاً ولو ذهبت عيناه يسقط من الدين بحساب العمياء فكذا هذا، لأن البنت لما جعلت بدلاً وتبعها للأم في الرهن فلو قامت الأم مقام البنت يكون في هذا المتبوع تبعاً لتبعيته وهذا خلاف موضوع الشرع فلا تقوم الأم مقام البنت بل تبقى أصلاً وتبقى رهناً أمة تساوي ألفاً بألف فولدت ولدين كل واحد يساوي ألفاً فجنى أحدهما كما كانت رهن فدفع ثم فقأت الأم عينه فدفعت الأم وأخذ الولد مكانها فالولدان بألف، وهذا عندهما لأن الابن الأعمى يقوم مقام الأم والأم مع الابن الصحيح كأنها رهناً الدين وكذلك بجميع الابنان. وعند محمد رحمه الله تعالى يسقط مع الدين بقدر نقصان الأعمى، فإن مات الأعمى
A female slave mortgaged for one thousand and worth one thousand gives birth to a son worth one thousand. The son injures someone and is handed over (as compensation). Nothing of the debt is void because handing over the son is like destruction; if the son died, no debt falls. Similarly here. If the mother gouges out the eyes of the daughter, and the mother is handed over and the daughter is taken, then she (daughter) is a pawn for the full thousand. Because if the mother dies, she dies according to both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad?). According to Muhammad, the debt falls by the amount of the defect of the eye, because in his view regarding a blind corpse: if the owner of the gouger chooses to hand over and take the corpse, he may do so, and the owner of the victim may not keep the corpse and claim the deficiency. Similarly, according to Abu Yusuf, if the owner of the victim chooses to hand over the corpse and take the gouger, the entire pawn is lost to a substitute, so the substitute stands in its place. According to Muhammad, the owner of the victim may keep the corpse and claim the deficiency, and the gouger is a substitute for the corpse and both eyes. So what corresponds to the eyes from the pawn has been voided because the eyes did not become property of the mortgagor nor reach the mortgagee. So the pawn is, to the extent of the corpse, lost to a substitute, so it becomes a pawn with it. If after that the mother gouges out the eyes of the daughter, and the mother is handed over and the daughter is taken blind, then in analogy she would be a pawn for the entire property because the daughter stood in the place of the mother by the handover, just as the mother stood in place of the daughter by the handover in the entire pawn. According to istihsan, the first pawn returns to its original state and is reduced by the amount of the deficiency of the eyes, because the mother was the original subject of the pawn, and the daughter was made a substitute and follower of her. When the mother is handed over for the daughter, the ability (to take the original) occurs before achieving the purpose of the pawn (payment of debt), so the consideration of the substitute falls, and the mother remains as the original pawn as before, not a substitute for the daughter. So if its eyes are lost, the debt falls by the amount of the blindness. Similarly here, because when the daughter was made a substitute and follower of the mother in the pawn, if the mother were to stand in the daughter's place, the followed would become a follower of its own follower, which is against the subject of the Sharia. So the mother does not stand in the daughter's place, but remains as the original. And a female slave worth one thousand by one thousand gives birth to two sons each worth one thousand; one injures as it was a pawn and is handed over; then the mother gouges out his eye; then the mother is handed over and the son is taken in her place, so both sons (together?) are for one thousand. This according to the two companions, because the blind son stands in the mother's place, and the mother with the healthy son is as if pawned for the debt, and similarly both sons. According to Muhammad, the debt falls by the amount of the deficiency of the blind one. Then the blind one died...
Source pages p. 503

Commentary
This extended passage presents several rulings and a known intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf (and commonly with Abu Hanifa). The scenario involves a mortgaged female slave (ama) worth 1000, debt 1000. She gives birth to a son worth 1000. The son commits an injury and is surrendered as compensation. The mother later blinds the daughter (perhaps the daughter of the same slave? The text is confusing: 'البنت' likely refers to the female offspring of the same ama? But earlier the son was born, now a daughter? Possibly the text is dealing with multiple offspring. The key dispute: when a substitute pawn (like a daughter handed over in place of the mother) is later subject to injury, does the original pawn (mother) revert to its original status? Muhammad says the substitute does not fully replace the original; the original remains in its original status, and any deficiency reduces the debt. Abu Yusuf holds that the substitute stands in the place of the original, so if the original is handed over for the substitute, the substitute becomes the pawn. This has practical implications for the mortgagee's security. The passage also discusses a similar case with two sons.

Key Terms
خلف (khalaf): Substitute; something that takes the place of the original pawn
استحسان (istihsān): Juristic preference overriding strict analogy (qiyas)
قياس (qiyās): Analogy: applying a rule from an original case to a new case due to shared cause

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, when a mortgagee takes a substitute pawn (e.g., a daughter) and later the original pawn (mother) is returned after being injured, what happens to the debt?
A) The debt is unaffected.
B) The debt is reduced by the deficiency caused by the injury.
C) The substitute remains the pawn.
D) The original pawn is void.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, there is a legitimate difference of opinion on whether a substitute pawn fully replaces the original or whether the original reverts upon return, affecting the debt's reduction for injury.

Handing Over a Pawned Slave for Injury: No Debt Reduction
Ruling with proof by qiyas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a pawned slave commits an injury and is handed over, and explain why no debt is reduced.

Core Idea
Handing over a pawned slave for his injury is like his death — the debt remains untouched.

This lesson examines a foundational rule in Hanafi pawnage law: when a pawned slave injures a third party and is handed over as compensation, the debt is not reduced. The reasoning is based on an analogy (qiyas) to the slave's death. We will trace the proof step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A pawned slave woman gives birth to a child; the child injures someone and is handed over to the victim.
The child is worth 1000, same as the mother.
2
Recognize the analogy
The handover is treated like the death of the child. If the child had died, no debt reduction. So handover has the same effect.
This is explicit in the text: 'دفع الولد بمنزلة الهلاك'.
3
Apply the ruling
Since handover is like death, no portion of the debt is nullified. The pawnage remains unchanged.
The debt remains 1000.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أمة مرهونة بألف وقيمتها ألف فولدت ولداً يساوي ألفاً فجنى الولد فدفع بها لم تبطل من الدين شيء لأن دفع الولد بمنزلة الهلاك، ولو هلك الولد لا يسقط شيء من الدين فكذا هذا وإن فقأت الأم عيني البنت فدفعت الأم وأخذت البنت فهي رهن بألف كاملة لأن الأم إن ماتت مات عندهما، وعند محمد رحمه الله تعالى يسقط من الدين بقدر نقصان العين لأن عنده في الجثة العمياء إذا اختار مولى الفاقئ الدفع وأخذ الجثة له ذلك، وليس لمولى المفقوءة إمساك الجثة يضمن النقصان، وكذلك عند أبي يوسف رحمه الله تعالى إذا اختار مولى المفقوءة دفع الجثة وأخذ الفاقئ فالرهن كله فات إلى خلف فيقوم الخلف مقامه وعند محمد رحمه الله تعالى لمولى المفقوءة إمساك الجثة ويضمن النقصان وكان الفاقئ بدلاً عن الجثة وعن العينين جميعاً فما بإزاء العينين من الرهن قد بطل لأن العينين لم تصر ملكاً للراهن ولا وصل إلى المرتهن فكان الرهن بقدر الجثة فائتاً بخلف فيكون رهناً به، فإن فقأت الأم بعد ذلك عيني البنت فدفعت وأخذت الأم عمياء ففي القياس تكون رهناً بجميع المال لأن البنت قامت مقام الأم بالدفع كما قامت الأم مقام البنت بالدفع في جميع الرهن. وفي الاستحسان يعود الرهن الأول على حاله ويذهب منه بحساب ما نقص من العينين لأن الأم كانت أصلاً في الرهن والبنت جعلت بدلاً عنها وتبعاً لها، فإذا دفعت الأم بالبنت فقد وقعت القدرة على الأصل قبل حصول المقصود بالبلد لأن المقصود من الرهن الإيفاء ولم يوجد الإيفاء فسقط اعتبار البدل فبقيت الأم أصلاً في الرهن كما كانت قبل الدفع لا بدلاً عن البنت فكانت أصلاً ولو ذهبت عيناه يسقط من الدين بحساب العمياء فكذا هذا، لأن البنت لما جعلت بدلاً وتبعها للأم في الرهن فلو قامت الأم مقام البنت يكون في هذا المتبوع تبعاً لتبعيته وهذا خلاف موضوع الشرع فلا تقوم الأم مقام البنت بل تبقى أصلاً وتبقى رهناً
A slave woman pawned for 1000 and her value is 1000, then she gave birth to a child worth 1000, then the child injured (someone) and was handed over (as compensation) — nothing of the debt is nullified because handing over the child is like its destruction; if the child had died, nothing of the debt would have been reduced, so likewise this. And if the mother poked out the eyes of the daughter, then the mother is handed over and the daughter is taken, she (the daughter) remains pawned for the full 1000 because the mother dies (in the sense of being handed over) according to them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). According to Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, part of the debt is reduced in proportion to the loss of the eye because in his view regarding a blind corpse: if the owner of the one who poked out eyes chooses to hand over (the offender) and take the corpse, he may do so, and the owner of the one whose eyes were poked out does not have the right to retain the corpse and claim compensation for the loss. Likewise according to Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, if the owner of the one whose eyes were poked out chooses to hand over the corpse and take the offender, then the entire pawnage is transferred to a substitute, and the substitute takes its place. According to Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, the owner of the one whose eyes were poked out may retain the corpse and claim compensation for the loss, and the offender becomes a substitute for the corpse and for both eyes, so whatever portion of the pawnage corresponded to the eyes is nullified because the eyes did not become the property of the pawner nor did they reach the pawnee; thus the pawnage remains to the extent of the corpse, which is lost but with a substitute, so it remains pawned accordingly. Then if the mother thereafter poked out the eyes of the daughter and is handed over, and the mother is taken blind, then by qiyas she remains pawned for the entire debt because the daughter took the place of the mother by handing over, just as the mother took the place of the daughter by handing over in the entire pawnage. By istihsan, the first pawnage returns to its original state, and from it goes in proportion to what was lost from the eyes because the mother was the original in the pawnage and the daughter was made a substitute for her and a follower of her. When the mother is handed over for the daughter, ability to access the original occurred before achieving the purpose in the country because the purpose of pawnage is repayment and repayment did not occur, so consideration of the substitute falls away, and the mother remains as the original in the pawnage as she was before the handover, not as a substitute for the daughter, so she is the original. And if his eyes go, there is a reduction from the debt in proportion to the blind (state), so likewise this. Because the daughter was made a substitute and a follower of the mother in the pawnage; if the mother were to take the place of the daughter, then in this case the followed thing would become a follower of its own follower, and this is contrary to the subject matter of the Law, so the mother does not take the place of the daughter; rather she remains the original and remains pawned.
Source pages p. 503

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on a complex scenario in pawnage (al-rahn). A slave woman (أمة) is pawned for a debt of 1000, and her value is also 1000. She gives birth to a child worth 1000. The child commits an injury (جناية) against a third party, and the child is handed over (يُدفع) as compensation (as a slave, not its value). The ruling states that handing over the child does not nullify any portion of the debt because it is equivalent to the child's destruction; if the child had died, no debt would be reduced, so the same applies here. Then, a new scenario: the mother pokes out (تفقأ) the eyes of the daughter. The mother is handed over as compensation, and the daughter is taken instead to be pawned. According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf ('عندهما'), the daughter becomes pawned for the full 1000 because the mother is considered 'dead' in terms of the pawnage (the mother leaves the pawnage). However, Imam Muhammad holds that the debt is reduced in proportion to the loss of the eyes because his position on a blind corpse (الجثة العمياء) differs: in his view, if the victim's owner chooses to hand over the offender (the mother) and take the blind corpse (the daughter), he may do so; the offender's owner cannot retain the corpse and demand compensation for the loss. For Abu Yusuf, if the victim's owner chooses to hand over the blind corpse and take the offender (the mother), the entire pawnage is transferred to a substitute (the mother) because the original pawned item (the daughter) is lost. But Imam Muhammad says the victim's owner may retain the blind corpse and claim compensation from the offender's owner. In this case, the mother becomes a substitute for both the daughter's body and eyes. The portion of the debt corresponding to the eyes is nullified because the eyes never became property of the pawner nor reached the pawnee; only the body (الجثة) remains pawned with a substitute (the mother). The passage then considers a second injury: after the first incident, the mother again pokes out the daughter's eyes. Now the daughter's eyelids are damaged? Actually, it says 'فقأت الأم بعد ذلك عيني البنت' meaning the mother pokes out the (new) daughter's eyes? Or is it the same daughter? It might be that after the substitution, the daughter (now pawned) has her eyes poked out by the mother (who was handed over). The mother is handed over again, and now the mother is taken blind. By qiyas, the blind mother would be pawned for the entire debt because the daughter had replaced her originally. However, by istihsan (juridical preference), the original pawnage (the mother) returns to its original state, and only the reduction for the blindness applies. The reasoning is that the mother was the original pawned item; the daughter was only a substitute and follower. Since the purpose of pawnage (repayment) was not achieved by handing over the daughter (she was not used to pay the debt), the substitute is disregarded, and the mother remains the original. Therefore, the mother cannot be treated as a substitute for the daughter; she remains the original pawned item, and the debt is reduced only in proportion to the loss of her eyes (as if she had gone blind). This illustrates the Hanafi principle: original items take precedence over substitutes when the purpose of pawnage remains unfulfilled.

Key Terms
رهن (rahn): A pawn or collateral given by a debtor to a creditor against a debt.
دفع (dafʿ): Handing over a slave as compensation for injury.
هلاك (halāk): Destruction or death; used as the basis for qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does handing over a pawned child for injury not reduce the debt?
A) Because the child is worthless.
B) Because handover is like death of the child.
C) Because the child is not owned by the pawner.
D) Because the injury was accidental.

Key Takeaway
Handing over a pawned slave for his injury is legally equivalent to his death — no debt is reduced.

When a Pawned Mother Blinds Her Daughter: Full vs Partial Substitution
Intra-Hanafi dispute with proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the substitution of a pawned slave when she blinds her daughter, and identify the positions of Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf vs Muhammad.

Core Idea
When a pawned mother blinds her daughter, do the daughter's eyes reduce the debt? The Hanafi masters differ: full substitution vs. proportional reduction.

This lesson delves into a nuanced intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. A pawned mother pokes out her daughter's eyes. The mother is handed over as compensation, and the daughter is taken as a substitute. Does the daughter become pawned for the full debt or less? Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say full; Muhammad says reduced for the eyes. Let's examine the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A pawned mother blinds her daughter. The mother is handed over as compensation; the daughter is taken into pawnage.
The mother's handover removes her from pawnage.
2
State the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
According to them (عندهما), the daughter becomes pawned for the full 1000 because the mother is considered 'dead' in pawnage.
They treat handover as complete loss of the mother.
3
State Muhammad's position
Muhammad holds that the debt is reduced proportionally to the loss of the eyes. The mother is a substitute for both body and eyes, but the eyes never became property of the pawner, so their portion of debt fails.
Muhammad allows the victim's owner to retain the blind corpse and claim compensation.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: Under Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf, the pawner still owes 1000; under Muhammad, the debt is less.
The mufta bihi is the majority view of the two shaykhs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أمة مرهونة بألف وقيمتها ألف فولدت ولداً يساوي ألفاً فجنى الولد فدفع بها لم تبطل من الدين شيء لأن دفع الولد بمنزلة الهلاك، ولو هلك الولد لا يسقط شيء من الدين فكذا هذا وإن فقأت الأم عيني البنت فدفعت الأم وأخذت البنت فهي رهن بألف كاملة لأن الأم إن ماتت مات عندهما، وعند محمد رحمه الله تعالى يسقط من الدين بقدر نقصان العين لأن عنده في الجثة العمياء إذا اختار مولى الفاقئ الدفع وأخذ الجثة له ذلك، وليس لمولى المفقوءة إمساك الجثة يضمن النقصان، وكذلك عند أبي يوسف رحمه الله تعالى إذا اختار مولى المفقوءة دفع الجثة وأخذ الفاقئ فالرهن كله فات إلى خلف فيقوم الخلف مقامه وعند محمد رحمه الله تعالى لمولى المفقوءة إمساك الجثة ويضمن النقصان وكان الفاقئ بدلاً عن الجثة وعن العينين جميعاً فما بإزاء العينين من الرهن قد بطل لأن العينين لم تصر ملكاً للراهن ولا وصل إلى المرتهن فكان الرهن بقدر الجثة فائتاً بخلف فيكون رهناً به، فإن فقأت الأم بعد ذلك عيني البنت فدفعت وأخذت الأم عمياء ففي القياس تكون رهناً بجميع المال لأن البنت قامت مقام الأم بالدفع كما قامت الأم مقام البنت بالدفع في جميع الرهن. وفي الاستحسان يعود الرهن الأول على حاله ويذهب منه بحساب ما نقص من العينين لأن الأم كانت أصلاً في الرهن والبنت جعلت بدلاً عنها وتبعاً لها، فإذا دفعت الأم بالبنت فقد وقعت القدرة على الأصل قبل حصول المقصود بالبلد لأن المقصود من الرهن الإيفاء ولم يوجد الإيفاء فسقط اعتبار البدل فبقيت الأم أصلاً في الرهن كما كانت قبل الدفع لا بدلاً عن البنت فكانت أصلاً ولو ذهبت عيناه يسقط من الدين بحساب العمياء فكذا هذا، لأن البنت لما جعلت بدلاً وتبعها للأم في الرهن فلو قامت الأم مقام البنت يكون في هذا المتبوع تبعاً لتبعيته وهذا خلاف موضوع الشرع فلا تقوم الأم مقام البنت بل تبقى أصلاً وتبقى رهناً
A slave woman pawned for 1000 and her value is 1000, then she gave birth to a child worth 1000, then the child injured (someone) and was handed over (as compensation) — nothing of the debt is nullified because handing over the child is like its destruction; if the child had died, nothing of the debt would have been reduced, so likewise this. And if the mother poked out the eyes of the daughter, then the mother is handed over and the daughter is taken, she (the daughter) remains pawned for the full 1000 because the mother dies (in the sense of being handed over) according to them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). According to Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, part of the debt is reduced in proportion to the loss of the eye because in his view regarding a blind corpse: if the owner of the one who poked out eyes chooses to hand over (the offender) and take the corpse, he may do so, and the owner of the one whose eyes were poked out does not have the right to retain the corpse and claim compensation for the loss. Likewise according to Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, if the owner of the one whose eyes were poked out chooses to hand over the corpse and take the offender, then the entire pawnage is transferred to a substitute, and the substitute takes its place. According to Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, the owner of the one whose eyes were poked out may retain the corpse and claim compensation for the loss, and the offender becomes a substitute for the corpse and for both eyes, so whatever portion of the pawnage corresponded to the eyes is nullified because the eyes did not become the property of the pawner nor did they reach the pawnee; thus the pawnage remains to the extent of the corpse, which is lost but with a substitute, so it remains pawned accordingly. Then if the mother thereafter poked out the eyes of the daughter and is handed over, and the mother is taken blind, then by qiyas she remains pawned for the entire debt because the daughter took the place of the mother by handing over, just as the mother took the place of the daughter by handing over in the entire pawnage. By istihsan, the first pawnage returns to its original state, and from it goes in proportion to what was lost from the eyes because the mother was the original in the pawnage and the daughter was made a substitute for her and a follower of her. When the mother is handed over for the daughter, ability to access the original occurred before achieving the purpose in the country because the purpose of pawnage is repayment and repayment did not occur, so consideration of the substitute falls away, and the mother remains as the original in the pawnage as she was before the handover, not as a substitute for the daughter, so she is the original. And if his eyes go, there is a reduction from the debt in proportion to the blind (state), so likewise this. Because the daughter was made a substitute and a follower of the mother in the pawnage; if the mother were to take the place of the daughter, then in this case the followed thing would become a follower of its own follower, and this is contrary to the subject matter of the Law, so the mother does not take the place of the daughter; rather she remains the original and remains pawned.
Source pages p. 503

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on a complex scenario in pawnage (al-rahn). A slave woman (أمة) is pawned for a debt of 1000, and her value is also 1000. She gives birth to a child worth 1000. The child commits an injury (جناية) against a third party, and the child is handed over (يُدفع) as compensation (as a slave, not its value). The ruling states that handing over the child does not nullify any portion of the debt because it is equivalent to the child's destruction; if the child had died, no debt would be reduced, so the same applies here. Then, a new scenario: the mother pokes out (تفقأ) the eyes of the daughter. The mother is handed over as compensation, and the daughter is taken instead to be pawned. According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf ('عندهما'), the daughter becomes pawned for the full 1000 because the mother is considered 'dead' in terms of the pawnage (the mother leaves the pawnage). However, Imam Muhammad holds that the debt is reduced in proportion to the loss of the eyes because his position on a blind corpse (الجثة العمياء) differs: in his view, if the victim's owner chooses to hand over the offender (the mother) and take the blind corpse (the daughter), he may do so; the offender's owner cannot retain the corpse and demand compensation for the loss. For Abu Yusuf, if the victim's owner chooses to hand over the blind corpse and take the offender (the mother), the entire pawnage is transferred to a substitute (the mother) because the original pawned item (the daughter) is lost. But Imam Muhammad says the victim's owner may retain the blind corpse and claim compensation from the offender's owner. In this case, the mother becomes a substitute for both the daughter's body and eyes. The portion of the debt corresponding to the eyes is nullified because the eyes never became property of the pawner nor reached the pawnee; only the body (الجثة) remains pawned with a substitute (the mother). The passage then considers a second injury: after the first incident, the mother again pokes out the daughter's eyes. Now the daughter's eyelids are damaged? Actually, it says 'فقأت الأم بعد ذلك عيني البنت' meaning the mother pokes out the (new) daughter's eyes? Or is it the same daughter? It might be that after the substitution, the daughter (now pawned) has her eyes poked out by the mother (who was handed over). The mother is handed over again, and now the mother is taken blind. By qiyas, the blind mother would be pawned for the entire debt because the daughter had replaced her originally. However, by istihsan (juridical preference), the original pawnage (the mother) returns to its original state, and only the reduction for the blindness applies. The reasoning is that the mother was the original pawned item; the daughter was only a substitute and follower. Since the purpose of pawnage (repayment) was not achieved by handing over the daughter (she was not used to pay the debt), the substitute is disregarded, and the mother remains the original. Therefore, the mother cannot be treated as a substitute for the daughter; she remains the original pawned item, and the debt is reduced only in proportion to the loss of her eyes (as if she had gone blind). This illustrates the Hanafi principle: original items take precedence over substitutes when the purpose of pawnage remains unfulfilled.

Key Terms
فقأ (faqa'a): To poke out (eyes).
جثة (juththa): Corpse or body (here of a living person after loss of eyes? Actually means the body of the victim after the eyes are poked out).
بدل (badal): Substitute that takes the place of the original pawned item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) between Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad in the mother-blinding-daughter scenario?
A) The daughter becomes pawned for the full debt vs. reduced debt.
B) The mother is freed vs. remains pawned.
C) The pawnage is void vs. valid.
D) The debt increases vs. decreases.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school internally disputes whether the substitute fully or partially replaces the original; the majority holds full substitution.

Istihsan Reverts the Substitute: The Original Prevails
Ruling with proof: qiyas vs. istihsan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the istihsan ruling regarding the reversion of the original pawned slave after a subsequent injury, and explain why qiyas is abandoned.

Core Idea
Qiyas says the substitute remains; istihsan restores the original because the pawner's purpose was not fulfilled.

In a second injury scenario, the mother again blinds the daughter and is handed over. By qiyas, the substitute (daughter) would continue, but by istihsan the original mother reverts, with reduction for her blindness. This demonstrates the Hanafi use of istihsan over qiyas when the purpose of pawnage is not achieved.

Guided Path
1
State the qiyas ruling
By qiyas, the blind mother would be pawned for the entire debt because the daughter had taken her place earlier.
The analogy is based on the previous substitution.
2
State the istihsan ruling
By istihsan, the original mother returns to pawnage, and the debt is reduced only for her blindness.
The substitute (daughter) is disregarded because the purpose of pawnage was not achieved.
3
Explain the reasoning for istihsan
The mother was the original (أصل); the daughter was merely a substitute (بدل). Since the debt was not repaid, the original remains valid. Making the mother a substitute for her own follower is contrary to legal structure.
Istihsan overrides qiyas to preserve the original arrangement.

Source Text

أمة مرهونة بألف وقيمتها ألف فولدت ولداً يساوي ألفاً فجنى الولد فدفع بها لم تبطل من الدين شيء لأن دفع الولد بمنزلة الهلاك، ولو هلك الولد لا يسقط شيء من الدين فكذا هذا وإن فقأت الأم عيني البنت فدفعت الأم وأخذت البنت فهي رهن بألف كاملة لأن الأم إن ماتت مات عندهما، وعند محمد رحمه الله تعالى يسقط من الدين بقدر نقصان العين لأن عنده في الجثة العمياء إذا اختار مولى الفاقئ الدفع وأخذ الجثة له ذلك، وليس لمولى المفقوءة إمساك الجثة يضمن النقصان، وكذلك عند أبي يوسف رحمه الله تعالى إذا اختار مولى المفقوءة دفع الجثة وأخذ الفاقئ فالرهن كله فات إلى خلف فيقوم الخلف مقامه وعند محمد رحمه الله تعالى لمولى المفقوءة إمساك الجثة ويضمن النقصان وكان الفاقئ بدلاً عن الجثة وعن العينين جميعاً فما بإزاء العينين من الرهن قد بطل لأن العينين لم تصر ملكاً للراهن ولا وصل إلى المرتهن فكان الرهن بقدر الجثة فائتاً بخلف فيكون رهناً به، فإن فقأت الأم بعد ذلك عيني البنت فدفعت وأخذت الأم عمياء ففي القياس تكون رهناً بجميع المال لأن البنت قامت مقام الأم بالدفع كما قامت الأم مقام البنت بالدفع في جميع الرهن. وفي الاستحسان يعود الرهن الأول على حاله ويذهب منه بحساب ما نقص من العينين لأن الأم كانت أصلاً في الرهن والبنت جعلت بدلاً عنها وتبعاً لها، فإذا دفعت الأم بالبنت فقد وقعت القدرة على الأصل قبل حصول المقصود بالبلد لأن المقصود من الرهن الإيفاء ولم يوجد الإيفاء فسقط اعتبار البدل فبقيت الأم أصلاً في الرهن كما كانت قبل الدفع لا بدلاً عن البنت فكانت أصلاً ولو ذهبت عيناه يسقط من الدين بحساب العمياء فكذا هذا، لأن البنت لما جعلت بدلاً وتبعها للأم في الرهن فلو قامت الأم مقام البنت يكون في هذا المتبوع تبعاً لتبعيته وهذا خلاف موضوع الشرع فلا تقوم الأم مقام البنت بل تبقى أصلاً وتبقى رهناً
A slave woman pawned for 1000 and her value is 1000, then she gave birth to a child worth 1000, then the child injured (someone) and was handed over (as compensation) — nothing of the debt is nullified because handing over the child is like its destruction; if the child had died, nothing of the debt would have been reduced, so likewise this. And if the mother poked out the eyes of the daughter, then the mother is handed over and the daughter is taken, she (the daughter) remains pawned for the full 1000 because the mother dies (in the sense of being handed over) according to them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). According to Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, part of the debt is reduced in proportion to the loss of the eye because in his view regarding a blind corpse: if the owner of the one who poked out eyes chooses to hand over (the offender) and take the corpse, he may do so, and the owner of the one whose eyes were poked out does not have the right to retain the corpse and claim compensation for the loss. Likewise according to Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, if the owner of the one whose eyes were poked out chooses to hand over the corpse and take the offender, then the entire pawnage is transferred to a substitute, and the substitute takes its place. According to Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, the owner of the one whose eyes were poked out may retain the corpse and claim compensation for the loss, and the offender becomes a substitute for the corpse and for both eyes, so whatever portion of the pawnage corresponded to the eyes is nullified because the eyes did not become the property of the pawner nor did they reach the pawnee; thus the pawnage remains to the extent of the corpse, which is lost but with a substitute, so it remains pawned accordingly. Then if the mother thereafter poked out the eyes of the daughter and is handed over, and the mother is taken blind, then by qiyas she remains pawned for the entire debt because the daughter took the place of the mother by handing over, just as the mother took the place of the daughter by handing over in the entire pawnage. By istihsan, the first pawnage returns to its original state, and from it goes in proportion to what was lost from the eyes because the mother was the original in the pawnage and the daughter was made a substitute for her and a follower of her. When the mother is handed over for the daughter, ability to access the original occurred before achieving the purpose in the country because the purpose of pawnage is repayment and repayment did not occur, so consideration of the substitute falls away, and the mother remains as the original in the pawnage as she was before the handover, not as a substitute for the daughter, so she is the original. And if his eyes go, there is a reduction from the debt in proportion to the blind (state), so likewise this. Because the daughter was made a substitute and a follower of the mother in the pawnage; if the mother were to take the place of the daughter, then in this case the followed thing would become a follower of its own follower, and this is contrary to the subject matter of the Law, so the mother does not take the place of the daughter; rather she remains the original and remains pawned.

قياس (qiyās): Analogical reasoning; the default method.

Pawned Mother with Two Children: Substitution and Debt Reduction
Ruling on a pawned mother with two children when injury and blinding occur.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the positions of Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad regarding debt reduction when a pawned slave is injured and replaced, and apply the principle of istihsan in such cases.

Core Idea
When a pawned slave is injured and replaced, the debt remains full per the majority, but is reduced under Imam Muhammad's view.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq examines a nuanced scenario in Hanafi pawnage law: a mother slave pawned for 1000 gives birth to two children each worth 1000. After one child injures someone, the mother blinds that child. The ruling hinges on whether the debt is reduced due to the child's blindness. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that the blind child replaces the mother fully, keeping the debt intact. Imam Muhammad argues for a proportional reduction. The passage also employs istihsan to return to the original pawnage in case of death. This lesson will help you navigate such intra-Hanafi differences and understand the application of istihsan over strict qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial pawnage setup
A slave woman worth 1000 is pawned for 1000. She gives birth to two children, each also worth 1000. One of these children commits an injury.
All values are equal to the debt amount.
2
Trace the sequence of events
The child who injured is handed over as compensation (still pawned). Then the mother pokes out that child's eye, blinding it. The mother is handed over as compensation for the blinding, and the blind child is taken in her place.
The blind child now stands in for the mother in the pawnage.
3
State the ruling of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
According to the majority, the two children (the blind one and the healthy one) together constitute the pawnage for the full 1000 debt. The blind son fully replaces the mother.
The phrase 'عندهما' indicates this is the position of the two imams.
4
State the ruling of Imam Muhammad
Imam Muhammad holds that the debt is reduced proportionally to the loss in value due to blindness. If the blind child dies, half the debt is gone.
This is a dissenting view within the Hanafi school.
5
Note the role of istihsan
If the remaining child (the healthy one) dies, istihsan returns the pawnage to its first state (the mother becomes the sole pawn), and the debt is reduced by the proportion of the mother's lost value. This overrides strict qiyas, which would keep the child as the pawn.
Istihsan is used to return to the original pawnage when the substitute is lost.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أمة تساوي ألفاً بألف فولدت ولدين كل واحد يساوي ألفاً فجنى أحدهما كما كانت رهن فدفع ثم فقأت الأم عينه فدفعت الأم وأخذ الولد مكانها فالولدان بألف، وهذا عندهما لأن الابن الأعمى يقوم مقام الأم والأم مع الابن الصحيح كأنها رهناً الدين وكذلك بجميع الابنان. وعند محمد رحمه الله تعالى يسقط مع الدين بقدر نقصان الأعمى، فإن مات الأعمى ذهب نصف الدين، فإن حتی الولد الباقي على الأم فدفع وأخذ عاد الرهن إلى حاله الأول وذهب من الدين بحساب ما ذهب من الأم استحساناً. وفي القياس يكون بما كان من الولد لما بينا
A slave woman worth 1000, pawned for 1000, gave birth to two children each worth 1000. One of them injured (someone) and was handed over as he was pawned. Then the mother poked out his eye, and the mother is handed over and the child is taken in her place. So the two children are (now) worth 1000. This is according to them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) because the blind son takes the place of the mother, and the mother together with the healthy son are as if pawned for the debt, and likewise with both sons. According to Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, part of the debt is reduced in proportion to the blindness of the blind one. If the blind one dies, half the debt goes. Then if the remaining child (is held) against the mother? (The text is unclear: 'فإن حتی الولد الباقي على الأم فدفع وأخذ') - if he is handed over and taken, the pawnage returns to its first state, and there goes from the debt in proportion to what went from the mother by istihsan. By qiyas, it would be as was with the child as we have stated.
Source pages p. 503

Commentary
This passage discusses a scenario involving a pawned slave woman who gives birth to two children, each valued at 1000 (same as the debt). One child commits an injury and is handed over as compensation, but he remains pawned (because he was part of the pawnage as a child of the pawned mother). Then the mother (the original pawned slave) pokes out the eye of that injured child (possibly the same one that was handed over, or the other? The text says 'عينه' referring to the one who injured). The mother is then handed over for poking out the eye, and the blind child is taken in her place to be pawned. According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf ('عندهما'), the two children (the blind one and the healthy one) together constitute the pawnage for 1000. The blind son stands in for the mother, and the mother is now with the healthy son as pawned for the debt. According to Imam Muhammad, the debt is reduced by the amount corresponding to the blindness of the blind child. If the blind child dies, half the debt is gone (because his value was half of the total pawnage? Actually careful: the debt is 1000, each child worth 1000, so the blind child's value after blindness might be less; Muhammad's position is that the debt decreases proportionally). The text then mentions 'فإن حتی الولد الباقي على الأم' which is likely 'فإن مات الولد الباقي على الأم' (if the remaining child dies while still with the mother). If that child is handed over and taken (as compensation for something), then the pawnage returns to its first state (the mother becomes the sole pawned item) and the debt is reduced by the proportion of what was lost from the mother (istihsan). By qiyas, it would remain as it was with the child (i.e., the child would be the substitute). This shows the Hanafi preference for returning to the original pawnage when possible.

Key Terms
أعمى (aʿmā): Blind; referring to a pawned slave who has lost his eyesight due to injury.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juridical preference that sets aside strict qiyas in favor of a more equitable ruling.
رَهْن (rahn): Pawnage; a contract where property is held as security for a debt.
أَمَة (amah): Female slave; in this context, the original pawned item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The debt is reduced by half.

C) The mother is freed from the pawnage.
D) The pawnage is void.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's majority holds that a substitute pawned item fully replaces the original without reducing the debt, while Imam Muhammad allows proportional reduction.

Injury Among Pawned Slaves: The Principle of Taba' and Debt Allocation
Rulings with detailed calculation for injury among pawned slaves.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on injury among pawned slaves, calculate the resulting debt shares, and explain the reasoning based on the principle of taba' (followership).

Core Idea
A pawned child is a follower of the mother; injury to the mother is like injury to own limb, but cross injuries involve complex debt reallocation.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a detailed case of two pawned slave women each with a child, all equal in value, and various scenarios of homicide among them. The rulings demonstrate how the principle of taba' (followership) nullifies compensation for certain injuries while requiring complex recalculation of debt shares for others. Mastering these calculations is essential for understanding pawnage transactions involving slaves.

Guided Path
1
Establish the initial debt structure
Note that the total debt is 1000, and the four slaves (two mothers, two children) are all worth 1000 each. Since values are equal, each is initially encumbered by 250 of the debt (quarter of total).
The debt is divided equally among the pawned slaves because the pawn contract apportions the debt based on their values.
2
Analyze the first scenario: child kills his own mother
Apply the principle that the child is a follower (taba') of the mother in pawnage. An injury by a follower upon the principal is like injury on one's own limb, hence it is hadar (invalid) – no compensation. The mother's death eliminates her share of the debt (250), and the child remains pawned for 250.
The child's status as a follower is derived from the fact that he became pawned only by following the mother; the pawn contract did not directly apply to him.
3
Analyze the second scenario: mother kills her own child
Here the mother's injury upon her child is also hadar, so the child's death is treated as natural. His share (250) returns to the mother, effectively increasing her encumbrance? Actually the text says 'returns to his mother' meaning the mother's share increases? More precisely, the child's share is freed from the pawnage and becomes the mother's property, but the debt allocation may shift. The key point: no compensation is due.
This scenario is simpler than the next.
4
Focus on the third scenario: one child kills the other child
Now the killer child (A) and the slain child (B) are both pawned, but A is not B's follower. Therefore, the injury is not automatically hadar. Break down B's value: three-quarters (750) is free of debt (since only 250 was encumbered), and one-quarter (250) is encumbered. The injury on the free part is hadar (it's destruction of free property by a pawned person, but the free part is not part of the pawn). The injury on the encumbered part must be further divided: one-quarter of the encumbered part (i.e., 1/4 of 250 = 62.5) is injury by the encumbered upon the encumbered – also hadar. The remaining three-quarters of the encumbered part (187.5) is injury by the free part of A upon the encumbered part of B – this is compensable.
This compensable portion shifts from B's debt to A's debt. Thus A now owes an additional 187.5, making his total debt 437.5.
5
Determine the final debt distribution after the killing
After the transfer, the total debt of 1000 is now split: A owes 437.5 (7/16), M_A owes 250 (4/16), M_B owes 250 (4/16), and the slain B's share is reduced? Actually B is dead, so his debt is eliminated except for the portion transferred to A. The text expresses the new shares in fractions: A is pawned for 1/8 + 1/16 = 3/16? Wait, the text says 'three from sixteen become one-eighth and half an eighth' – likely means 3/16. Then the rest is 'six-eighths and half an eighth' = 6.5/8 = 13/16. This is confusing but the point is the debt is reallocated.
The fractions ensure the total remains 1000. The exact fractions may require careful fractional arithmetic.
6
Consider post-event deaths: killer dies, killer's mother dies, victim's mother dies
If the killer dies, no debt reduction because his death is like natural death of a pawned child – nothing drops. If his mother dies, her share (250) drops (quarter of total debt). If the victim's mother dies, her share (250) plus an additional 62.5 (1/8 of 500) for the injury on her child drops – total 312.5, which the text says is 'five-eighths of 500' (4/8 = 250 for her own debt, 1/8 = 62.5 for the injury portion).
These reductions illustrate how the debt diminishes when the owners (the mothers) die.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رهن أمتين تساوي كل واحدة ألفاً فولدت كل واحدة ولداً يساوي ألفاً، ثم إن أحد الولدين قتل أمه لم يلحقه من الجناية شيء وكان رهناً بمائتين وخمسين وذهبت الأم بما فيها مائتين وخمسين لأن جناية ولد الرهن على الأم هدر لأنه تبع للأم وفي حق الرهن لأن عقد الرهن لم يرد عليه وإنما صار رهناً تبعاً للأم فصار كسائر أطرافها وجنايتها على طرفها هدر فسقط ما فيها فكذا هذا ولو أن الأم قتلت ولدها عاد نصيبه إليها لأن جنايتها على ولدها إن كانت مهدرة صار كأن الولد مات حتف أنفه ويخلف ما فيه إلى أمه، ولو لم يكن كذلك لكن أحد الولدين قتل الولد الآخر كانت أم المقتول وثلاثة أثمان القاتل رهناً بخمسمائة وخمسة أثمان القاتل وأمه رهن بخمسمائة قال : والصواب أن يقال بأن ثمن القاتل ونصف ثمنه أم المقتول رهناً بخمسمائة وستة أثمان القاتل ونصف أم القاتل بخمسمائة لأن الدين انقسم بينهم أرباعاً لاستواء قيمتهم فصار بإزاء كل واحد منهم مائتان وخمسون وثلاثة أرباع المقتول فارغ عن الدين لأن قيمته ألف وربعه مشغول والقاتل كذلك والجناية على ثلاثة أرباع الفارغ هدر والجناية على ربع الربع المشغول هدر لأنه تلف بجناية المشغول على المشغول فيتحول ما بإزائه إلى أم المقتول وذلك اثنان وستون ونصف والجناية على ثلاثة أرباع هذا الربع معتبرة لأنه تلف بجناية الفارغ على المشغول فيتحول ما بإزائه إلى القاتل وذلك مائة وسبعة وثمانون ونصف وذلك ثلاثة أرباع مائتين وخمسين فصار ما في المقتول وهو مائتان وخمسون على اربعة أسهم فصار الألف على ستة أسهم وقد تحول ثلاثة منها إلى القاتل وثلاثة من ستة عشر يكون ثمنه ونصف ثمنه والباقي ستة أثمان ونصف ثمنه، فإن مات القاتل لم يسقط من الدين شيء لأنه بهلاك ولد الرهن لا يسقط شيء، فإن لم يمت وماتت أمه ذهب ربع الدين لأنه كان بإزائها ربع الدين، ولو لم تمت أمه ولكن ماتت أم المقتول ذهب من الدين خمسة أثمان خمسمائة أربعة أثمانها دين نفسها وهو مائتان وخمسون وثمنها بسبب الجناية على ولدها وبقي القاتل رهناً بسبعة أثمان خمسمائة أربعة أثمان دين نفسها وذلك مائتان وخمسون وثلاثة أثمان تحول إليه من دين المقتول وذلك مائة وسبعة وثمانون ونصف وخمسون ومائتان في عتق فيفتكهم به الراهن
Two pawned slave women each worth 1000, each gave birth to a child worth 1000. Then one of the children killed his mother: nothing from the injury attaches to him, and he remains pawned for 250, and the mother goes with her (share) of 250 because the injury of a pawned child upon its mother is invalid (hader) because he is a follower of the mother, and regarding the pawnage, the contract of pawnage did not apply to him but he became pawned as a follower of the mother, so he is like one of her limbs, and injury upon her limb is invalid, so what was in her falls away. So likewise this. If the mother killed her child, his share returns to her because her injury upon her child is invalid; it is as if the child died a natural death, and what was in him passes to his mother. If it is not like that, but one child killed the other child, then the mother of the slain and three-eighths of the killer are pawned for 500, and five-eighths of the killer and his mother are pawned for 500. He (the author) said: The correct view is that an eighth of the killer and half of his eighth (i.e., 1/8 + 1/16) and the mother of the slain are pawned for 500, and six-eighths of the killer and half of the killer's mother (i.e., 6/8 + 1/2) are pawned for 500 because the debt was divided among them in quarters due to the equality of their values. So each one of them had 250 against him. Three-quarters of the slain are free of debt because his value is 1000, and one quarter is encumbered. Likewise for the killer. The injury upon three-quarters of the free (portion) is invalid, and the injury upon a quarter of the quarter encumbered is invalid because it is destruction by the encumbered upon the encumbered, so what was in exchange for it shifts to the mother of the slain, that being 62.5. And the injury upon three-quarters of this quarter is considered because it is destruction by the free upon the encumbered, so what was in exchange for it shifts to the killer, that being 187.5, which is three-quarters of 250. So what was in the slain, which is 250, becomes upon four shares, so the 1000 becomes upon six shares. Three of them have shifted to the killer, and three sixteenths of that? Actually the text: 'وثلاثة من ستة عشر يكون ثمنه ونصف ثمنه والباقي ستة أثمان ونصف ثمنه' (three sixteenths become one-eighth and half of an eighth, and the remainder is six-eighths and half of an eighth). If the killer dies, nothing of the debt drops because with the destruction of a pawned child nothing drops. If he does not die but his mother dies, a quarter of the debt goes because she corresponded to a quarter of the debt. If his mother does not die but the mother of the slain dies, five-eighths of 500 go: four-eighths of that is her own debt which is 250, and one-eighth is due to the injury on her child. And the killer remains pawned for seven-eighths of 500: four-eighths of that is his own debt which is 250, and three-eighths shifted to him from the debt of the slain, that being 187.5, and 50 and 200 in emancipation? The final portion: 'وخمسون ومائتان في عتق فيفتكهم به الراهن' (and 50 and 200 in manumission? The pawnor ransoms them with it).
